Many Western Merchants Also Oppose Phone Rate Increases

The Hua Dong News Agency reports that the Shanghai Concession Telephone Company's rate increase plan is based on the company's slight losses in the past and its failure to reach a dividend rate of one point last year. Therefore, there is a proposal to increase prices. After the company submitted this proposal to the Public Works Department, the board of directors is considering it. According to the agreement between the company and the Public Works Department, the telephone rate increase may not exceed 25%. Therefore, the current rate of increase is 22%, with private telephones increasing from 7 yuan, 5 jiao, and 8 fen per month to 8 yuan and 5 jiao, and business telephones decreasing from 12 yuan and 4 jiao to 10 yuan. However, the latter is limited to 100 calls per month, with a charge of 3 fen per call for exceeding the limit. Yesterday, a Public Works Department board member informally told a Hua Dong News Agency reporter that the matter is currently being discussed by the Public Works Department board of directors. After careful study by the foreign directors, they believe that the reasons are sufficient, (?) so they are likely to agree in principle. If so, the telephone rate increase may be implemented on April 1st.

Increased Rate Surplus

A Hua Dong News Agency reporter has learned that the Telephone Company estimates that after the rate increase is implemented, the number of calls made per month may be reduced by 50%. After the number of calls is reduced, the annual surplus will be 1,523,750 yuan. However, according to speculation from foreign business circles in this city, the number of calls will definitely not decrease after the telephone rate increase. This is because people are now only making calls that are necessary. Very few people are intentionally making extra calls. If the Telephone Company can achieve such a large surplus with a 50% reduction in calls, then the actual annual surplus should be double the Telephone Company's estimate, i.e., 3,047,500 yuan. At the same time, for this reason, people who want to borrow a phone to make calls will not be able to do so and will have to use public telephones. Therefore, the number of public telephone calls will also increase more than before, and the Telephone Company can earn more revenue, it is said.

Westerners Oppose

There is considerable opposition to the Telephone Company's rate increase in the city because it harms business and is unaffordable. There is also opposition from the Western community. Yesterday, the Shanghai Eacuange Brokers Association sent a letter to the Public Works Department board of directors requesting a rate reduction. The association also sent letters to various Chinese groups to gain sympathy. It is reported that the members of the association have a total of 900 lines. If the rate is increased, the losses will be significant, it is said.

The Zhejiang Provincial Department of Construction, in order to save the silk industry in Zhejiang Province, implemented control measures during the autumn cocoon season last year and stipulated various methods to restrict silk merchants from outside the province from collecting cocoons, resulting in the interruption of raw materials for various silk factories in the city, which successively suspended work. Resolution: The general membership meeting will be held at the Hangzhou Business Federation at 1:00 PM on March 32nd. Resolution: Recommend Chen Zhexian to draft a proposal, submit it to the general meeting for approval, and then issue it. Two representatives from the Jiangshan County Relief Branch in Zhejiang, Yang Dezhong and Zhu Weichuan, came to the Chinese and Foreign Relief Association on Rue Nanking yesterday to request relief and presented a handwritten letter from Mr. Xiong Xiling. A copy is recorded below: "To whom it may concern, Jiangshan County, Zhejiang Province, suffered a particularly severe drought last year and was also ravaged by communist troops, making it particularly tragic. I recently returned to the county to visit relatives and witnessed the disaster, which I cannot bear. I am hereby submitting a report for your review. The county is located on the frontier and lacks publicity, so few people know the truth. Therefore, most of the groups providing relief are in Hangzhou, Jiaxing, Huzhou, Ningbo, Shaoxing, and Taizhou, while only Xiaoshan County is in Jinhua, Quzhou, and Yanzhou. Jiangshan County is left out in the cold, which is very pitiful. Please provide assistance so that the disaster victims in the county can celebrate their rebirth. The merits will be immeasurable. [Signed] Xiong Xiling." Enclosed in the letter was a disaster report from Taijun, which is lengthy and omitted. It mentions that the disaster situation in the county, especially in Quzhou, is severe. Local disaster victims have exhausted their supply of bracken roots and are about to run out of food. They may not be able to survive until the wheat harvest. It is also heard that the Chinese and Foreign Relief Association, recognizing the severe droughts in Jiangshan, Changshan, and Longyou, allocated 5,000 yuan last winter for emergency relief, which is a drop in the bucket and has been going on for a long time. Therefore, the spring famine is self-evident. However, all the association's relief funds have reportedly been allocated, making it difficult to cope, which is quite hesitant. However, it is hoped that all sectors will provide assistance to save these dying disaster victims.

Jardine Spinning Mill Labor Dispute Resolved: Party and Government Mediation Results in Workers Resuming Work Soon

The Old Jardine Spinning Mill on Yangshupu Road in Eastern Shanghai and the New Jardine Mill on Weituoma Road employ over 11,000 workers. Due to the depressed yarn market, the factory decided through a shareholders' meeting to reduce all wages by 10%, leading to a reaction from all workers. Starting on the 24th of last month, strikes occurred successively. Although the Communist Party and government authorities sent personnel to mediate, no results were achieved as both sides held their ground. The situation has been turbulent in recent days and the situation is quite serious. The local Party and government authorities in Shanghai, concerned that the stalemate in the Jardine labor dispute was detrimental to local security, dispatched Li Weixiong from the Municipal Party Committee, along with Zhang Chuqiang from the Social Affairs Bureau, to the factory again yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM to conduct mediation. They summoned contractors Zhang Gensheng, Zhang Rongsheng, Ding Rongkun, etc., from the factory to inquire about the situation. Three solutions were then drafted: (1) Wages should be paid in full, with small silver dollars discounted at the full rate; (2) The contractors should come forward to welcome all workers back to work; (3) After this labor dispute is resolved, the contractors will guarantee that the factory will not dismiss any workers. The above solutions have been fully accepted by the contractors. It was originally scheduled to officially resume work yesterday. However, as the engine room and other departments in the factory still need to be organized, a formal announcement will be made by the factory to all workers to return to work after the organization is completed. It is expected to be resolved within two or three days.

Shanghai Overseas Chinese Affairs Bureau Plans to Establish an Overseas Chinese Affairs Office

Jian Jinglun, Director of the Shanghai Overseas Chinese Affairs Bureau, has been actively handling overseas Chinese affairs in the city recently. He recently published the bureau's work and facility plans for this year. The main focus is on establishing a job placement center for unemployed returning overseas Chinese. Yesterday (the 14th), he convened a bureau meeting of all bureau staff to discuss relief and guidance measures, deciding on two matters: (1) It is proposed to establish an Overseas Chinese Affairs Office. The bureau believes that the number of overseas Chinese going abroad and returning to the country is increasing daily. Overseas Chinese have been away from the country for a long time and often have little knowledge of the domestic situation, making them vulnerable to deception by local thugs. The bureau plans to submit a request to the Nanjing Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission to petition the Ministry of Finance to approve the establishment of an Overseas Chinese Affairs Office inside the Jianghai Customs Wharf, dispatching staff to work there permanently to provide consultation and guidance to overseas Chinese, so that they will not be deceived. (2) To publish an Overseas Chinese magazine and convenient pamphlets. In addition to making efforts to guide returning overseas Chinese and promote overseas Chinese affairs, the bureau is still concerned about omissions and will roughly follow the methods of travel guides, listing detailed Shanghai concise maps and main transportation routes, as well as introductions to various major industries, commercial companies, factories, and clan associations. This publication will be carried out in cooperation with the Seamen's Union, asking crew members to distribute it widely so that all overseas Chinese know where to inquire.

Car Accident on the Shanghai-Minhang Road: Chen Adi Killed, Car Owner Flees

On the 9th of this month, Chen Jingeng, who lives in Qiaojiaqiao, Fengxian, and suffers from epilepsy, had a son named Adi, only fourteen years old, who supported his elderly father by selling green onions and vegetables. On that day, he collected wolfberries and took them to Xinzhuang to sell. At about 3:00 PM, while returning past the Chang'an Cemetery, he was suddenly hit from behind by a car with license number 643 in the city and license number 5421 in the concession, which was speeding. He died instantly. This was witnessed by Li Rusong, an employee of the Chang'an Cemetery. The car owner, knowing that he had caused an accident, quickly drove to Minhang and abandoned the car by the riverbank, immediately fleeing with his servant. After an inspection by the Shanghai Local Court, it was confirmed to be true and an order was issued to prepare the body for burial and await the arrest of the perpetrator. Now, Chen Jingeng is heartbroken over the loss of his son and his old illness has relapsed. He is extremely miserable. It is now reported that he has also reported to the Pudong Fellow Villagers Association, asking for assistance to seek justice as soon as possible.

An Old Man and a Young Man Die Pitiably

The Shanghai Local Procuratorate reported yesterday afternoon that Jiang Pingyang, the head of the ninth ward, reported that there was a pit latrine in the Liu Tomb Alley in the nine acres of land. An old man went to the latrine the previous night. Somehow, he suddenly fell to the ground, barely breathing. Wang Amao, who was guarding the latrine, saw this and was shocked. He tried to rescue him but was unsuccessful, and he died soon after. Subsequently, a passerby claimed that the deceased was named Xia Jinsheng, 60 years old, and lived at No. 10 Gaoxing Lane, Tangjiawan. He was a coppersmith. The case is within the jurisdiction of the map, and it is appropriate to request an autopsy and burial. Also, Zhuang Hongkui, the security officer of the 24th ward and 20th district, reported that there was a young man about 17 or 18 years old in Yangjing West Town, Pudong. He had a dignified appearance, but was poorly dressed and suffered from a serious illness, lying on the road. Kind people asked him his age, place of origin, whether he had any family members, and why he came here. He claimed to be from Tongzhou. His father traded in Ningbo. This time, he was ordered by his mother to come to Shanghai from his original home to take a boat to Ningbo to find his father. Unexpectedly, due to his youth and carelessness, he was robbed of all the meager travel expenses he was carrying, leaving him in a dilemma and stranded in Shanghai. Unfortunately, due to his bad fate, he was also afflicted with illness. After speaking, his eyes were full of tears and his expression was extremely miserable, causing those who saw him to feel distressed. When asked for the detailed address of his hometown, he was unable to speak, only shaking his head repeatedly. People tried to send him to the hospital for treatment. However, the young man's illness was incurable and he was taken to a wasteland in Xiliukou in the town at about 8:00 AM yesterday to be temporarily placed, and he died soon after. Please conduct an autopsy, etc. For the above two cases, Prosecutor Wu Ying led examiner Xuan Zhiming and others to the scene to conduct an examination and confirmed that both had died of illness. An order was issued for coffins and burials.

Ruan Lingyu's Funeral Yesterday

Ruan Lingyu's remains were taken from the Wanguo Funeral Home on Jiaozhou Road at noon yesterday, arriving at the Lianyi Villa in Zhabei at about 3:00 PM. The funeral was held at 4:30 PM. When the funeral procession passed through various roads, many people stood and watched silently. The various events before and after yesterday's funeral are recorded below in detail:

Crowds of Tens of Thousands on Jiaozhou Road

Since Ruan Lingyu's body was placed in a coffin on the 11th, the total number of people who went to the Wanguo Funeral Home to pay their respects reached more than 100,000. Upon hearing the news that Ruan's coffin would soon be transported to the cemetery for burial, no fewer than tens of thousands of people gathered in the Jiaozhou Road area yesterday. The police station in charge of the area also anticipated that the crowds would definitely be crowded, so they specially dispatched a large number of detectives to protect the scene, and there were also many mounted patrols to clear the traffic routes. Before noon, the section of Jiaozhou Road, Avenue Road, and Connaught Road was closed to traffic, and even pedestrians were refused passage.

Relatives and Friends Went in Groups to Hold the Funeral Rope

In the morning, Ruan's coffin was still open, and relatives and friends who went to the funeral frequently went to pay their respects. Ruan's remains were slightly thinner and yellower than before, but still beautiful. There were many male and female relatives and friends from the Tang and Ruan families in the mourning hall. At about 12:10 PM, those who went to hold the funeral rope had gathered on the lawn in front of the mourning hall. It is estimated that more than 300 employees and friends from Lianhua and various film companies arrived. At one time, it was very solemn and solemn. First, a Taoist priest played cymbals to perform a religious service. Then, twelve employees from Lianhua Company and two Westerners jointly carried the coffin onto the hearse. It was led by a large horizontal banner with the words "Funeral of Artist Ruan Lingyu" written on white bamboo cloth with black edges, and the Shanghai Orphanage's full orchestra, and a hearse with a large photograph of Ruan, about six or seven feet high. Due to the restrictions of the police station, only 30 funeral cars were allowed. They departed at 2:00 PM and were still protected by a large number of detectives along the way until they passed the Xinqiao Shipyard.

Streets Blocked as the Hearse Passed

When the coffin reached Hengfeng Road from Jiaozhou Road, the streets were completely blocked by people and vehicles. After reaching North Baoxing Road, the traffic began to be slightly smoother. However, those who went to Lianyi Villa on foot or by car were continuously reaching several miles away.

Lush Cemetery: Artist Rests in Peace Forever

At about 4:00 PM, the coffin arrived at Lianyi Villa. The portrait was moved into the Lianyi Hall. Those holding the funeral rope were treated to tea and snacks by the Tang residence. At that time, thousands of people had already arrived. The villa is a public cemetery run by a Cantonese man. The path is quite wide and there are many gardens and a sense of tranquility. In addition, it is early spring. The grassy fields, green willows, and red peaches seem very suitable for the long sleep of an artist. Ruan's tomb is located in the north. It is expanded with cement and is about two feet deep. Before Ruan's coffin entered the tomb, it was originally planned to open the coffin for a final viewing, but because there were too many onlookers at the time, it was feared that order could not be maintained, and it did not happen. It was immediately covered with stone slabs and sealed with cement. The funeral was then completed.

Homicide Occurs in Western Shanghai: Elder Brother Stabs Younger Brother to Death Over a Boxwood Tree

At about 8:00 PM yesterday, Liu Qiancheng, the police chief of the Sandaodi Police Station of the Xujiahui Police Station in western Shanghai, was patrolling with the police when he heard cries for help in the Panjiazhai area on the eastern side of the Zhongshan Road Railway. He immediately followed the sound and found many villagers. When asked about the situation, he learned that Qian Fugeng, a local resident living at No. 39 Panjiazhai and engaged in flower cultivation, and his younger brother, Qian Anan, had fought fiercely over a boxwood tree. Both men were now injured and lying by the river. Police Chief Liu saw that Qian Anan's injuries were very serious, and Qian Fugeng's head was also injured. He took the two men by car to the Chinese Red Cross Hospital on Haige Road for treatment. However, Anan suffered two stab wounds in his chest, penetrating deep into his lungs. He died soon after without being able to be saved. The hospital notified the Xuhui Police Station, which took the murderer Qian Fugeng back to the station and detained him. At the interrogation conducted by the station chief yesterday, Qian Fugeng confessed that he was 34 years old and that the deceased was his younger brother, 29 years old. Today, his younger brother sawed off a boxwood tree planted in his garden. His mother, Ding, tried to stop him but he refused to listen and insulted his mother. His mother was angry and cried. He went home and learned about it. He reasoned with his younger brother, but it angered him. He struck his head with a rasp. He fled. Unexpectedly, the deceased chased after him and accidentally fell to the ground, causing the rasp to stab his chest. He did not hit him. After the station chief took the confession, he sent a document to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for investigation, as the case involved human life.

Shanghai-Hangzhou Freight Train Derails at Xinlonghua Station: Three Cars Overturn, One Section of Steel Rail Damaged, Soldiers and Escort Police Injured

The 801st freight train from Shanghai to Hangzhou on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway, scheduled to depart from Maigen Road Station every day, arrives at Xinlonghua Station at 10:15 AM to wait for freight cars from South Station and Richun Port Station to connect and drive to Hangzhou. Unexpectedly, at 11:25 AM yesterday, when the 801st freight train was turning around at Xinlonghua Station, because the freight cars from Maigen Road Station, totaling four cars, had not yet driven out of the No. 8 branch line, the driver did not notice the backward movement, causing it to collide with the freight cars from South Station due to insufficient avoidance. As a result, three of the four freight cars overturned, numbered 6169 and 60811, two heavy cars, and the 6144th car loaded with military supplies was also derailed at the seventh branch line, and a section of steel rail on the third track was damaged. Chen Guidong, a soldier of the machine gun company of the 589th Regiment of the 95th Brigade of the 19th Division of the Army, and Sun Huchen, an escort policeman from the Jiaza section of the railway, who were escorting military supplies in the 6144th freight car, were slightly injured on the car. They were diagnosed and bandaged by the South Station Medical Office. Fortunately, the station could pass through the first track for traffic and there was no obstacle. After the accident, the station chief urgently telegraphed the North Station's Transportation, Works, and Machinery Departments, asking them to send a rescue vehicle to provide assistance. Zhong Wenjiang, the chief of the South Station Transportation Section, accompanied by Luo, an engineer from the Engineering Department, and Han Shangying, the chief of the Police Section, led workers and others, and at 12:05 PM, they took the handcar to Xinlonghua to investigate. At 3:00 PM in the afternoon, a rescue vehicle was sent from the North Station Machinery Department to Xinlonghua Station to carry out repairs separately. The goods that had been overturned in the freight car were unloaded by laborers. The damaged steel rails were then replaced, and the derailed and overturned freight car was jacked onto the track using a crane. It was completely repaired by about 8:00 PM last night and traffic was restored. Therefore, the 801st freight train was delayed until about 9:00 PM before it started to depart for Hangzhou.

Egg Exports Suffer a Sharp Decline: Proposed Tax Increase in the United States Not Yet Implemented, Egg Prices Plunge, Annual Loss of 10 Million, Hoping the Government Will Exempt Taxes to Enhance Competitiveness

Guowen News Agency reports that China's egg industry is suffering internally from the impact of rural bankruptcy and externally from tariff barriers in various countries, resulting in a deteriorating situation for exports. Although the quantity has increased, the value has fallen to an irredeemable level. There are quite a few egg merchants in Shanghai, most of whom are small-scale operations. Only about 30 large egg merchants belong to the trade association. China's fresh eggs are usually exported from Shanghai, Tianjin, Qingdao, and Hankou. The annual export volume is very large, with a value of about tens of millions of dollars, making it one of the rural sideline industries. Recently, someone in the United States has proposed to Congress to increase taxes on Chinese eggs. At the same time, our Minister Shi also filed a protest. The reporter inquired with local egg merchants yesterday and recorded the details as follows:

Source of Egg Products: Fresh eggs mainly come from Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hubei, Henan, Shandong, and other provinces. They are collected by small vendors in the interior and transported to Shanghai, Hankou, Tianjin, Qingdao, and other ports for export. The total export volume last year was 1.6 million dan. Approximately 40 million dan were sold directly in the country. Last summer, due to the drought, agricultural crops were affected, and the feed for chickens and ducks naturally became a problem. Therefore, since last year, the source of eggs from the famous egg-producing areas along the Yangtze River has also been greatly reduced. In addition, due to export restrictions, egg prices have plummeted. The total loss due to the price drop in the past year is more than 10 million dollars.

Egg Prices Plunge: In previous years, the prices of fresh eggs in the interior varied from season to season. In spring, each dan was from 20 to 17 or 18 dollars. In summer, it was from 15 or 16 to 17 or 18 dollars. In autumn and winter, due to slightly larger consumption, the price was from 20 to 27 or 28 dollars. However, in recent years, it has been only 14 or 15 dollars in spring, 11 or 12 dollars in summer, and smaller eggs are only 8 or 9 dollars per dan. Although autumn and winter are peak seasons, the price is only 15 or 16 to 21 or 22 dollars. The reasons for this are the infighting among the trade and the restrictions in foreign markets.

Sharp Decline in Exports: Among China's egg exports, the largest volume comes from Tianjin, followed by Shanghai, then Qingdao, and then Hankou. Eggs are generally divided into fresh eggs (chicken and duck), water eggs (including whole eggs, egg yolks, and egg whites), dried eggs, wet eggs, colored eggs, salted eggs, frozen eggs, etc. They are exported to Singapore, the United States, Italy, France, Germany, Japan, Belgium, Denmark, the Netherlands, Australia, the Philippines, Singapore, and other places. The annual business is quite considerable. In 1920, the total export value was more than 79.7 million, but last year it was only more than 30.2 million, a difference of more than one time. The following table shows the export volume and total value of China's egg products in the most recent two years:

Year Water, Wet, and Dried Egg Products Fresh, Colored, and Salted Eggs Total Value

1933 47,315 tons 354,662 pieces 36,079,624 yuan

1934 49,474 tons 319,545 pieces 30,243,526 yuan

U.S. Increases Egg Tax: It was previously reported that the United States plans to increase tariffs on Chinese egg imports. The reporter asked egg merchants and they said they only saw the report that U.S. congressmen had proposed it to Congress, and our ambassador to the United States also filed a protest. It is not yet known whether it will be implemented. As for the amount of Chinese eggs exported to the United States, according to last year's customs statistics, from January to November, the total amount of dried egg whites and yolks, as well as wet egg yolks, was 14,052 metric tons. There are no accurate statistics for fresh, colored, and salted eggs, so they are not included. The number is of course considerable. If the United States actually increases taxes, then we will have another layer of losses. Therefore, at this time of decline in the egg industry, what is hoped for from the government is that it can immediately exempt egg export taxes. What is hoped for from the trade is sincere cooperation, otherwise it will be difficult to compete in the international market and it will be difficult to avoid following in the footsteps of our country's silk and tea.

Industrial Decline: Workers' Livelihoods are Precarious: Workers of Shenxin No. 5 Factory Demand the Factory Open, Workers of Meikang Silk Factory Oppose Second Wage Reduction

The workers of Shenxin No. 5 Factory petitioned the Social Affairs Bureau yesterday morning to open the factory due to livelihood reasons. The workers of the Meikang Silk Factory also petitioned the authorities to oppose the company's wage reduction. The details are as follows:

Shenxin No. 5 Factory: The Shenxin Textile Company's No. 5 Factory at 1316 Huade Road has more than 1,000 workers. The factory has not started work since it stopped work before the final accounting, and it is difficult to maintain a livelihood. They have petitioned the authorities, instructing the company to open the factory as soon as possible so that they can work. Wang Xianqing, a staff member of the Third Section, received them and promised to send staff to investigate and mediate.

Meikang Silk Factory: The Meikang Silk Factory on Haizhou Road, Yangshupu, has more than 150 workers, divided into day and night shifts. Since the factory started work this year, it has stopped opening the night shift and announced that wages for piecework workers will be paid at 70% of the original rate, and those paid by the day will have their wages reduced by 5 to 7 cents per day. All workers said that the factory had already reduced wages once in August last year, and now the factory is reducing wages again, making it difficult to maintain a livelihood. They sent representative Lu Zuguang to negotiate with the company, but there was no result, and he was fired by the company. Therefore, the workers sent representatives to submit a petition to the Party and government authorities for negotiation. The Social Affairs Bureau has sent mediator Zhang Chuqiang to investigate the truth.

Yuan Ludeng Repays Debts on Behalf of Others: Couple Reconciles; Judge Persuades for Half an Hour, Record of Court Settlement Achieved

Zhou Ruitang, a native of Ningbo and junior proprietor of Zhou Lin Ji Clock & Watch Wholesale located at No. 15 Yuxing Lane, Nanjing Road, married Lu Sujuan, a woman from the same hometown, in March of the 16th year of the Republic of China through the introduction of Yuan Ludeng and others. After their marriage, they initially lived harmoniously and had a son. However, disagreements arose, and Lu returned to her mother's home in Ningbo, where she worked as a teacher in a church school to support herself. In total, they were married for eight years, but lived together for only two years and six months. Now, Zhou suddenly engaged a lawyer to file a suit in the First Special District Court, requesting a divorce from Lu. Lu also engaged lawyer Tang Youwei to file a counterclaim, demanding cohabitation and ordering Zhou to repay the seven hundred yuan in debts she had incurred outside in recent years. Judge Zhang Qinglan of the First Special Court had already held a hearing once, summoning them and advising them to reach an out-of-court settlement. These details were previously reported in this newspaper. Yesterday, Judge Zhang continued the hearing in the Fourth Civil Court, and Yuan Ludeng was also summoned to court to testify. Judge Zhang first summoned both the plaintiff and the defendant to the court, persuading them to reconcile. He repeatedly advised them, hoping that both parties would reconcile and continue to cohabit. Zhou seemed willing to agree to cohabitation, but was unwilling to repay Lu's debts, as she had left on her own. The judge told him that if he treated Lu Sujuan with sincerity, she would definitely not leave without a reason. Even though she had been living with her mother for the past few years, he should still provide for her livelihood. Therefore, this debt should be repaid on his behalf. However, Zhou firmly refused. Judge Zhang repeatedly advised him for half an hour, but Zhou insisted on refusing. The court then summoned Yuan Ludeng to the stand. According to Yuan, he and both the plaintiff and the defendant were family friends. There was no major animosity between the two parties, only stubbornness in their personalities, which led to today's events. He had once mediated a reconciliation, enabling both parties to reconcile unconditionally and avoid a rift. As for the debt owed by the woman, he would repay it on her behalf, and the man's parents would certainly repay him in full in the future. One day, he had invited both parties to dinner at his home, intending to have them return home together after the meal, so that both parties could save face. However, Zhou Ruitang did not arrive in time, so it was unsuccessful. Today, the only dispute is over the one hundred yuan debt. If he could bear this expense, a reconciliation could still be achieved. Judge Zhang deeply agreed with his statement and immediately summoned the two parties to further persuade them. Both the plaintiff and the defendant expressed their willingness to accept the court's advice and Yuan Ludeng's mediation plan, to reconcile and continue to cohabit. Judge Zhang further urged them to respect and love each other as husband and wife in the future, and not to act impulsively again, so that their future happiness would be boundless. After finishing his advice, he made a record of the settlement, which was signed by both parties, and then the court adjourned. This scene of a husband and wife cross-suing each other thus came to an end.

Chief Prosecutor Zheng Yue of the Second Branch of the High Court Held Inauguration Ceremony Yesterday

Zheng Yue, Chief Prosecutor of the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court, who arrived last month, held his official inauguration ceremony at 3:00 PM yesterday in the reception room behind the First Court of the Second Branch. Chief Zheng had previously invited representatives from various party, government, military, police, and judicial organizations in the city to attend the ceremony, and the Judicial Administration Department sent Shen Jiayi, President of the Second Branch of the High Court, to supervise the oath. The ceremony was grand and magnificent. The details are as follows:

Hall Arrangement: The hall was located in the reception room behind the First Court on the ground floor of the Second Branch of the High Court. The portrait and will of Sun Yat-sen were hung on the wall, along with crossed party and national flags. On both sides were party songs, oaths, and a table of ceremony order. The right side was for the supervisor, oath-taker, and party representatives, and the rest was for the guests. The hall area was not very spacious, but the arrangement was very elegant and tidy. The words "Hall" were written on the door for identification. The party and national flags were hung above the main gate of the court, and the national emblem was also displayed on the roof. The guest sign-in area was set up in the corridor at the entrance. After signing in, guests were warmly guided upstairs by staff wearing red ribbons to the reception room for tea and refreshments.

Guest Sign-In: After 1:00 PM, guests arrived at the court one after another, including Mao Yun from the Municipal Party Headquarters, Chen Hanzuo representing the Garrison Command, Deng Peiyi representing the Municipal Security Office, Shen Xiqing, President of the Shanghai District Court, Zhong Shangbin, Chief Prosecutor of the court, Tang Zaili representing the Third Branch of the High Court and the First Special District Court, Ren Yi, Warden of the Model Prison, Sun Xiong, Deputy Warden, Guo Yunguan, President of the First Special District Court, Xiang Zhejiong, Chief Prosecutor, He Dekui of the Municipal Council, Gan Jingxian, Lawyer of the Municipal Council, Shen Junru, representative of the Shanghai Bar Association, and court presidents, judges, prosecutors, and journalists from the First Special District and the Second Branch of the High Court, totaling fifty or sixty people, filling the seats.

Inauguration Ritual: (1) The supervisor takes the presiding seat, (2) the oath-taker takes his place, (3) everyone stands at attention, (4) sings the party song, (5) pays the highest respects to the national flag, party flag, and Sun Yat-sen portrait, (6) the chairman respectfully reads Sun Yat-sen's will, (7) three minutes of silence, (8) oath, (9) supervisor's instruction, (10) party representative's speech, (11) guests' speeches, (12) oath-taker's reply, (13) end of the ceremony.

Oath Transcription: I solemnly swear that I will strictly abide by Sun Yat-sen's will, obey party principles, abide by laws and regulations, be loyal and diligent in my duties. I resolve not to waste a single penny, not to misuse a single person, and never to engage in embezzlement or bribery. If I violate this oath, I am willing to be subject to the most severe punishment. This oath.

Speech Outline: As the bell rang three times, the supervisor, oath-taker, guests, etc., slowly entered the hall and performed the ceremony as scheduled. Then, President Shen delivered a speech on behalf of the Ministry of Justice, saying that the duties of a prosecutor are nothing more than investigating crimes, filing public prosecutions, and executing judgments. But what is particularly important is the reporting of corruption and perversion of the law. If he abides by party principles, abides by laws and regulations, does not waste a single penny, does not misuse a single person, and never engages in embezzlement or bribery, he must practice what he preaches. Chief Zheng has always been honest and upright, and will certainly be able to fulfill his responsibilities and uncover evil. Then, Mao Yun, representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters, delivered a speech, saying that modern law is progressing day by day, and now we have good judges to enforce the law, represent the country in enforcing the law, and will certainly increase glory in the international arena and bring a unique color to the judiciary. Next, He Dekui gave a speech, and finally Zheng Yue replied, saying that due to the restrictions of agreements with foreign powers, he will do his best within his ability, and dare not be negligent. He is honored to receive the guidance of the supervisor and the teachings of all the guests, and hopes to receive more advice in the future to assist him.

Bandit Opened Fire to Resist Arrest and Was Shot Dead

On Rue Grosseille in the French Concession, at approximately 11:45 PM last night, a wonton vendor was calling for customers by striking his clapper on the roadside. Suddenly, a man came and ate a bowl of plain noodles. After finishing, he said to the vendor, "Do you have any copper coins to change?" While the vendor was taking money, the man suddenly grabbed the money and fled westward. After seeing this, the vendor, reluctant to let anyone snatch away his hard-earned money, shouted "Robber!" At that time, a patrol team of four French police officers happened to be passing by in a car, including a French policeman, two Vietnamese policemen, and a Chinese policeman. Upon hearing the cry for help, they chased after him. When they were near Rue Roll, no more than a few feet away, the thug took out a gun from his sleeve and fired at the police. Fortunately, it did not hit them. The police then fired back one after another, firing five or six bullets in a row, all hitting the bandit's vital parts. He immediately fell to the ground and died. The gun held by the thief was discarded on the roadside. After the police searched for it, they took it to the police station for filing. The corpse was sent to the Tongren Fuyuan Hall. This morning, the court was notified to examine the body.

(2) Prices In terms of prices, the wholesale price index and retail price index of the Gold Bloc countries have consistently shown a downward trend in recent years, with the most significant decline occurring in 1932. The impact of price drops on industrial production is undoubtedly significant.

(3) Production In terms of production, we can gain insight from the industrial production index of the Gold Bloc countries (1928 equals 100). In 1930, the indices of all countries except France declined. In 1931, they all declined uniformly. In 1932, the drop was even more severe, with the highest being 75.6 for France and the lowest being 63.9 for the Netherlands. Subsequently, although there was a slight improvement in 1933, it trended downwards again in 1934, except for Italy. Looking solely at the current year, the Italian index showed a sharp upward trend throughout the year. The Belgian index remained largely unchanged. The Netherlands saw its index rise above 79 in February and May of the first half of the year, but it then suffered a setback starting in June, falling to a low of 62 in September. The November index was only 63.9. The average index for the 11 months of the year was 70.9, similar to 1933. The French index showed a consistently straight downward trend throughout the year, starting at 83.5 in January and falling to 78.0 in June. The lowest point was 74.0 in October and November. The average index for the 11 months of 1934 was 78.4.

(1) Average of indices from January to November for the entire year.

(4) Unemployment and Bankruptcies The rise and fall of unemployment and bankruptcy indices best illustrate the state of the social economy. Statistics on unemployment and bankruptcies in the Gold Bloc countries have shown an increasing trend since 1929, with the most significant increase occurring in 1932. Although unemployment and bankruptcy statistics in Italy and the Netherlands showed a slight decrease in 1934, they were still significantly higher than in 1931 and earlier. France, which had seen a slight decrease in 1933, experienced an increase again this year, reaching the highest record in recent years. The number of unemployed people increased from only 10,052 in 1929 to over 376,386 in 1934. The average monthly number of bankruptcies increased from 726 in 1929 to 1,214 in 1934. The increasing social burden and frequent business failures are hidden worries for the future of economic recovery.

Spring and Autumn

Snippets

— (Xu Haowu)

The health of the body lies in the blood; the turmoil of society lies in money.

Blood must circulate; money is called currency. Local congestion will cause local or global organizational obstructions, which is not a good phenomenon.

Colorful banknotes carry the same bloody odor. The difference is that the rich indulge in wine and women, and what they take without end is mostly the flesh and blood of others. They don't have the same poignant and pungent smell of sweat and blood that the poor exchange for their earnings while groaning and lamenting.

Because money is coagulated blood, gangsters use blood to represent money, and ordinary people regard money as blood. With money, even strangers are treated like sons; without money, one's own parents are treated like servants.

Money is blood; flies suck it up without hesitation. Are humans just the embodiment of flies?

The Oldest Soup Kitchen

— Shijiu

It is already mid-spring, and soup kitchens everywhere are either closing down or about to close down. This reminds me of the soup kitchen in Rugao County, Jiangsu—the oldest soup kitchen in our country.

The Rugao soup kitchen has a history of two to three hundred years, dating back to the Ming Dynasty. The kitchen has been able to operate until now thanks to the enthusiastic contributions of kind people, who donate rice or money. Rugao has always been known as "Golden Rugao." If you see a man on the street wearing a blue cloth skirt around his waist, don't laugh at him as an old man. He may have tens of thousands in assets, and that's a very common thing. Since there are so many wealthy people, it's not surprising that they would donate four or five hundred yuan to the soup kitchen. The most commendable thing is the staff who run the soup kitchen. They have no desire to profit or embezzle donations. Otherwise, with an anonymous donor donating 300 yuan and an undisclosed donor donating 500 yuan, it would be impossible to verify if they were embezzling funds, because the kind people of Rugao are unwilling to reveal their real names when making donations.

Every winter, poor people within fifty miles of the city load their entire families into boats and row to the vicinity of the soup kitchen to moor. They can sit and eat for three months. The soup kitchen does not refuse anyone. Therefore, when the north wind rises, the small boats in front of the soup kitchen are connected end to end, stretching for several miles, like a long serpent formation, which can be considered a spectacle. This cannot be done without a substantial soup fund!

The act of dispensing soup, if considered according to the principle of "benevolent governance without relief," may seem inappropriate. However, it is, after all, the intention of benevolent people, and the meaning cannot be faulted too much. Like the soup kitchen in Rugao, which has been able to continue for two to three hundred years, it is quite commendable.

Jiang Kanghu's Discussion of Romance of the Three Kingdoms

— Zheng Mei

Dr. Jiang Kanghu lives in Qingliang Temple in Xin's Garden, not far from my residence, so I often have the opportunity to seek his counsel. The doctor knew that I was compiling "The Complete Romance of the Three Kingdoms," so he spoke about his feelings regarding Romance of the Three Kingdoms, which were quite witty and meaningful. Therefore, I recorded them on the left:

"I once read Records of the Three Kingdoms and felt that the Three Kingdoms period was truly a time of abundant Chinese talent! Wise rulers, virtuous ministers, brave generals, and resourceful strategists existed in each country. The talents of any one country were sufficient to turn chaos into order, achieve unification, and bring about peace. However, they ultimately failed because the other two countries also had comparable and equal talents, creating mutually offsetting and dissipating efforts. If the talents of the Three Kingdoms had been combined, the Eastern Han Dynasty would have been revived long ago. Even if any two countries had formed alliances to control the third country, the warfare would not have been so dramatic and prolonged. Therefore, each of the Three Kingdoms had talent, and the talent was divided among the Three Kingdoms, which means that Heaven did not want to bring peace to the world! I once again read Romance of the Three Kingdoms and felt even more deeply that the Three Kingdoms period was truly prosperous. However, the reason why the names and deeds of the figures are well-known to every household, familiar, and detailed is due to the popularizing power of Romance of the Three Kingdoms. Before the Three Kingdoms, there were the Spring and Autumn and Warring States periods, which were not without talents similar to those of the Three Kingdoms. After the Three Kingdoms, there were the Six Dynasties and Five Dynasties, which were also not without talents similar to those of the Three Kingdoms. However, without a historical novel like Romance of the Three Kingdoms, their talents were alienated from the minds and eyes of the general populace, and the influence of their names and deeds on customs and society was limited. The effect of historical novels is great! Romance of the Three Kingdoms, based on historical materials and incorporating anecdotes, is a masterpiece crafted with originality."

After Dr. Jiang said this, he added that my compilation of the complete work, encompassing all aspects, not only benefits Records of the Three Kingdoms and Romance of the Three Kingdoms, but also serves as a good friend for those who read Records of the Three Kingdoms and Romance of the Three Kingdoms. How unfortunate it is that talents were born in the Three Kingdoms, where they were undermined and excluded, unable to fully realize their strengths! How fortunate it is that talents were born in the Three Kingdoms, where they were recorded by famous historians and depicted by famous novelists, so that they still possess a vivid spirit after thousands of years! My work further expands their legacy and can be attached to Chen Shou and Luo Guanzhong and become immortal. He used words of encouragement that I dared not accept.

Spring Plowing

— Jiang Mi

Little Western Paradise

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 10: Abruptly Revealing Wealth Before a Young Lady to Entice Her, Coveting Her Through Gaps in the Wall, Worrying About Her Chastity

Zhang Jiefu also joined in, saying, "That's right! Master Jia has plenty of money, he doesn't care about this little bit. You can take it." This was truly beyond the dreams of Zhu Hu's wife, who immediately bent over and gave him two bows. Yueying, who had never received such great kindness, unfolded her tightly furrowed brows and smiled at Jia Duocai, saying, "Thank you very much. Poor people can only benefit from gentlemen like you." Jia Duocai never expected that once the money had changed hands, he would be able to make jokes, so he followed behind and walked out of the room, whispering, "See, am I not a very easy-going person? If you spend more time with me, you'll know that I'm the easiest person to talk to." Yueying looked at him, then lowered her head and smiled slightly, pursing her lower lip and gently biting it with her teeth. Jia Duocai had a particular fondness for seeing women in such a shy state. Yueying's doing this bewitched him somewhat. When Zhu Hu's wife came out, following Yueying, he followed Yueying as well. Zhang Jiefu was just standing there idly. The host had left, and the guests had left, so what was the point of him standing there? Therefore, seeing Jia Duocai following Zhu Hu's wife and daughter, he didn't want to disturb them, so he quietly returned to his room. At this time, only the two stacks of foreign money remained in Jia Duocai's room, guarding the table, and it was relatively quiet. However, in the darkness, there was a person whose emotions were particularly tense. It turned out that the room was partitioned with wooden boards. Although they were fitted together very neatly, there were gaps due to the age of the construction. In that room, lived a woman who was bored and had found a book on counting dominoes, which she was reading under the light. The sound of the conversation on the other side reached her ears, and she was very surprised, feeling that this was clearly a human flesh trade. When it came to making money, who wouldn't want to do something like that? (157)

Records of Imperial Incense

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

Actually, I had long known how a woman later revered as "Leizu" in ancient times taught people the story of raising silkworms, but what the Empress Dowager said was a bit more special. What she said was:

"In ancient times, there was a girl who one day suddenly found a silkworm. She thought it was very interesting, so she caught it and put it in a box, but later forgot about it. After three or four days, she suddenly thought of it again, and hurriedly opened the box to take a look, but the silkworm was gone. She saw only a white oval thing. She didn't have the mind to study it carefully, so she took it out and played with it. Her parents saw it and were also very surprised. Of course, there was no such name as 'cocoon' at that time, but after carefully playing with it, they discovered that there was silk on this thing that could be drawn out, and they thought of the possibility of using silk. They then went out together with the girl to look for more. Because they often found them on mulberry leaves, they determined that mulberry leaves were the food for silkworms. From then on, the business of raising silkworms and reeling silk gradually improved and developed. Today, almost half of the fields in our Chinese territory are planted with mulberry trees. In various villages, there are special temples dedicated to this girl. Silkworm-raising families go to pray every year, hoping that she can bless their silkworms to produce good cocoons. This girl has thus become a famous figure in Chinese history."

I don't know if what the Empress Dowager said is reliable, or if other legends are reliable? However, Leizu is indeed a highly revered inventor in our Chinese history. (268)

Shoes

— Yan Chonglou

Late at night, when I was taking off my shoes, I suddenly noticed a crack in the side of one of the shoes.

"The shoe is broken!" With a sigh, some thoughts arose in my mind:

When I first went to the shoe store, I chose this pair of shoes from among many. It was a pair that fit just right. The tough leather shone with a bright luster. Wearing them on my feet drew the attention of many people to my feet.

The shoes followed me every day, running east and west. Sometimes their surfaces inevitably got dusty. I would wipe them with a flannel cloth, apply some shoe polish, and brush them. Then they would be brand new again.

But as time went by, when it rained, the shoes also followed my feet on muddy roads. The tough leather was inevitably soaked in mud and water, and the bright luster was inevitably covered by dirt. Although I continued to clean them, they could no longer attract attention like they used to.

Now, not only are the heels of these shoes worn down, but I've also noticed a crack in the edge. They are no longer usable. They will be handed over to the maid and become discarded items in the trash can—

The shoes were destroyed in the process of helping me live my life. They never uttered a word of complaint. But towards these shoes that helped me—these shoes that helped me walk many roads—when I see them leaving me forever, can I not have a little bit of lingering affection?

Acknowledgments Shou Kai Tang Ji, written by Mr. Zhou Yansheng of Nantong. Mr. Zhou's given name is Jialu, a distinguished tribute student of the Qing Dynasty Haimen Subprefecture. In the late Qing Dynasty, both Shen Wensu Gong and Wu Wuzhuang Gong specially invited Mr. Zhou to be their staff members. His poems and essays were as famous as those of Fan Dangshi, Zhang Jian, Gu Xijue, Zhu Mingpan, and other famous scholars in the county at the time. In addition to dedicating himself to poetry and prose, he also excelled in textual research and collation. He wrote thirteen works, including Interpretations of Classics, History, and Poetry, Verification of the Meaning of Words, Collation Notes on Records of the Three Kingdoms, Haimen Subprefecture Gazetteer, and Comprehensive Compilation of Records of Korea, totaling 101 volumes, all rich in profound and insightful ideas. Shou Kai Tang Ji is one of them. This book is divided into eight volumes and imitates Song-style collection of treasures. It is not only rich in literary talent but also meticulously printed, truly a masterpiece in the literary world of modern China. The reference department of this library has received a complimentary copy from Mr. Ji Cheng, and we express our special thanks.

Miscellaneous Talk

Changes in Wedding Attire During the Republican Era

— Nangong Sheng

The changes in clothing over our country's five thousand years are countless. Generally, after the establishment of a new dynasty, there must be regulations regarding clothing and decoration, especially for wedding attire, which is highly valued and has a set system. However, the wedding attire of a new dynasty is only officially regulated after a change of regime. Therefore, for hundreds of years, wedding attire did not change as frequently as everyday clothing.

Since the establishment of the Republic of China, the system for formal attire has been undecided and frequently reformed. As a result, wedding attire has also changed with the times and lacks consistency. Since 1935, the differences in wedding attire have varied from month to year, which is very different from the one-style-per-dynasty system of the past. This is all due to the lack of defined formal attire. In summary, from the first year of the Republic to the present day, the evolution of wedding attire can be roughly divided into the following types, which are briefly described below.

In the first year of the Republic, because the Qing Dynasty had abdicated not long before, the dress code was undecided. People only knew that the Qing Dynasty's mandarin jacket was not suitable for wedding attire, but there was no fixed formal attire format, and they didn't know what to follow. Thus, wedding attire followed local customs. Generally, the groom wore a long gown and a dark outer jacket, with the color of the gown fabric being light and bright. The bride still wore a red skirt and cape, similar to the Qing Dynasty. This was the earliest wedding attire shortly after the establishment of the Republic.

Later, brides all knew that the cape and red skirt were not in line with the times, but without a formal attire style, they imitated European and American dress, wearing Western-style clothes, with pink as the preferred color, and a beaded veil. The length did not reach the ground. The groom still wore a long gown and a dark outer jacket with a melon-rind cap. This was the most popular attire in 1913 and 1914. After this era, brides switched back to ordinary-style dresses, in pink or bright red, wearing a beaded crown. The groom favored a small and fashionable look, with narrow-sleeved and small-front gowns and jackets, which were popular for weddings. This lasted for about two to three years.

Around 1919 and 1920, the bride's attire began to have a formal style, which was a short, mandarin-collar jacket embroidered with a coiled dragon or crane pattern, extending to the knees. Red was used for weddings, and other colors, such as Tianjin blue, were used at other times. A red skirt, also embroidered with floral branches, was worn underneath. Pink or bright red was used for weddings, while bright red was used at other times. A beaded crown was worn on the head, with pendants covering the face, and a beaded veil was draped over it. Flowers were held during the wedding. The groom's attire included both long gowns and dark outer jackets with melon-rind caps, and Western-style formal wear. The Western-style was worn with a tall top hat. All weddings generally followed one of these styles.

Up to today, the cheongsam has been designated as women's formal attire, and wedding attire is primarily based on the cheongsam. However, there are variations with short or long sleeves, and specially made ones. The color is mostly pink, and the beaded veil drags on the ground for several feet. The groom's formal attire is a blue gown and dark outer jacket with a melon-rind cap. However, due to the popularity of Western suits in recent years, Western-style formal wear is often used as wedding attire, and the blue gown and dark outer jacket mandated by the government are rarely seen. This is all due to the times and customs.

Education News

Siam: After the Suppression of Overseas Chinese Education

Luo Wanli Recently Reported the Truth; Overseas Chinese Federation Asks the Government to Negotiate

(Central News Agency, Nanjing, 14th) The Siamese government, due to the suppression of overseas Chinese schools, caused dissatisfaction among overseas Chinese. Recently, the Siamese Minister of Education, Bachasarasai, intended to find another solution and invited Lin Tianduo, the principal of Jiao Guang Middle School in Shantou, to contribute his opinions. Lin sent a letter to Bachasarasai at the end of last month, detailing the improvement methods.

(Nanjing, 13th) Luo Wanli recently returned to Nanjing from Siam. When reporters inquired about the truth of Siam's suppression of overseas Chinese education, he said that since the success of the revolution in Siam in 1931, the People's Party came to power and promulgated education regulations, which have been implemented for three years. Recently, they have intensified their efforts, arbitrarily banning overseas Chinese schools, or closing and taking back the school agency rights of overseas Chinese schools, and saying that if there is resistance, they will use guns and knives to solve it, even at the cost of lives. As for the rescue methods, it depends on the efforts of the government and the overseas Chinese in Siam. The issue of overseas Chinese education itself should adopt what policy, and it is urgent to discuss it.

The Overseas Chinese Joint Research Association felt that the overseas Chinese education in Siam has been repeatedly suppressed and telegraphed the government yesterday as follows: To Wang, President of the Executive Yuan of the Nanjing National Government, and Chen Jun, Chairman of the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission, our overseas Chinese compatriots in Siam number more than one million. In recent years, they have suffered greatly due to the extreme oppression of the local government. In addition to restricting the entry of Chinese people and strictly enforcing compulsory education regulations, they have recently issued an order to suspend Chinese people within a limited time. Schools and cultural institutions established in Siam, and the government is ignoring our country. If the government does not seriously negotiate and allow it to be trampled on, the future of overseas Chinese education will be unimaginable. It is a matter of national security and the safety of the nation. We earnestly request that you quickly ask the government to seriously negotiate to demand the improvement of overseas Chinese education and promote Sino-Siamese relations in order to appease the feelings of overseas Chinese and benefit the people. The Overseas Chinese Joint Research Association bowed humbly.

International Competition for Sports Films

Held in Berlin on September 10th

The Chinese Educational Film Association recently received a letter from the Rome International Educational Film Association, stating that at the International Educational Film Conference held in Rome last year, a proposal was made to encourage the production and promotion of sports films. The original text stated, "The International Educational Film Conference believes that encouraging the production and promotion of sports films is extremely effective and uses the 11th Summer Olympics in 1936 as a good opportunity. Therefore, it is proposed to create an International Competition for Sports Films to achieve the purpose of awarding and promoting such films. This competition is organized by the International Educational Film Association and will be held in the autumn of 1935. To make this plan effective, the International Conference proposes that the Summer Olympics International Committee award gold medals to the best sports films at the 1936 Olympic Games, following the precedent of the committee's awards for the best works on sports. It is also hoped that the representatives of the countries attending the meeting will promptly notify the representatives of the Summer Olympics Committee in their respective countries so that they can submit it for discussion. The Italian Prime Minister has always been enthusiastic about sports and exercise and is invited to support this proposal so that this case can achieve satisfactory results." After the case was passed by all members, it was sent to the Summer Olympics International Committee and submitted for discussion at the 31st meeting held in Athens. The meeting believed that the International Educational Film Association paid attention to promoting the work of films on sports in the process of developing educational films, which was greatly appreciated and unanimously passed to fully support the cause of the International Educational Film Association. As for the proposed organization of the competition, it was also strongly approved. The International Educational Film Association has been actively preparing for the competition by the association's technical and advisory committee. The regulations for the competition have been formulated with a total of fourteen articles: (1) The first International Competition will be initiated and hosted by the International Educational Film Association and organized by the association's technical and advisory committee based on the decision made at the meeting in Stresa in 1934 to select the best sports films. (2) Film production companies, private filmmakers, and film artists, regardless of nationality, may submit their works to participate in the competition. (3) The films participating in the competition are limited to those filmed from 1932 to the autumn of this year. (4) The subject matter of the film should be limited to various sports, without excluding any kind, such as gymnastics, track and field, swimming, rowing, football, basketball, tennis, baseball, skiing, cross-country running, and others. Films that are not filmed on-site but are falsely produced shall not be allowed to participate. Only the various forms of the sport itself, or some special forms, can be the main component of the film and the actions of the performance. (5) One first, second, and third prize will be awarded according to the order of classification. (6) Each competition shall be composed of an executive committee established by the technical and advisory committee of the International Educational Film Association to judge during the inspection and selection of films. The chairman of the executive committee shall be the representative of the country hosting the Summer Olympics. The president of the International Educational Film Association is an ex officio member. In addition, official representatives of seven countries including Italy, France, England, Germany, Russia, Japan, and the United States are all ex officio members. (7) The affairs of the competition will be handled by the chairman of the executive committee. (8) The honorary committee is composed of members of the executive committee and one representative from each country participating in the competition. Sports and motion figures may also be invited to participate in the honorary committee, but the right to choose candidates is purely in the hands of the executive committee. (9) The judgments of the executive committee shall be decided by a majority vote. In case of a tie, the vote of the president of the International Educational Film Association shall prevail. The results of the judgment shall be final and no changes may be requested. (10) Any country wishing to participate in the competition with its own films must pay a registration fee of 100 lire to the executive committee. The income from this item will be used to purchase medals and certificates for the best films. (11) The permanent secretariat of the competition is located at the International Educational Film Association, Via Lazzaro Spallanzani, Rome. (12) The country and city where the competition will be held shall be designated by the executive committee each time. The first competition was decided to be held in Berlin because the next Summer Olympics will be held in Germany in 1936. The director of the German National Film Bureau is the chairman of the executive committee of the first competition. (13) The judging meeting of the first competition is scheduled for September 10 to 20, 1935. (14) The winning films are still owned by the participating companies or manufacturers. The executive committee and the International Educational Film Association reserve the right to publish the results of the competition in newspapers and recommend the most effective methods for promoting these films in international sports centers to the winning companies and manufacturers.

The International Educational Film Association attaches great importance to this initiative and believes that it is a kind of appropriate ideal with educational and social significance, and uses physical sports as various principles of healthy sportsmanship, so it hopes that the associations of various countries will cooperate with it so that local film groups, production companies, filmmakers, or film artists can actively participate in the competition. After receiving the news, the Chinese Educational Film Association rushed to translate the original text and hoped that those in China who have such sports films would send them for participation as much as possible, but for the ex officio members of the executive committee, they are the seven major powers, and China is not among them, because our country's domestic film industry is not strong, and the promotion of educational films has only been around for three years, and there are very few products, which have not been promoted abroad, so in the future, we hope to work hard to make films and strive for international status.

Lianhua Factory Creates Three-Wheel Swimsuits

Swimming is a good way to stay healthy and a good way to pass the time in the summer. In recent years, swimming has become popular in our country in the summer. As a result, the number of swimming pools open during the season has been increasing year by year. The number of foreign-made swimsuits sold each year is very large. However, since the introduction of the three-wheel swimsuit, improvements have been made in the actual comfort of clothing during exercise and the propulsion of water resistance during swimming, reducing the waste of energy. The factory has conducted thorough research, so the number of athletes and swimmers who purchase and use them each year has been increasing, recovering a lot of profits. It is reported that the factory's latest 1935-style swimming suit has been created, including one style for men, one style for women, and one style for children. The wool body is made of chemically processed raw materials, so the problems of hygiene, water resistance, color fastness, and durability are all very practical.

Finance: Gold Market Weakens and Then Becomes Firm Again

April Forward Contracts: Central Bank Willing to Settle at Parity Early, Leading to a More Bullish Spread, Resulting in a Rise of Half a Yuan

The gold market yesterday was stimulated by news that the Central Bank urgently needed to ship spot goods for export and was willing to settle its previously purchased April futures contracts at parity half a month early, sparking buying interest. The market was weak and then became firm again, ultimately rising instead. At the start of the morning, overseas silver markets rose, with London up six pence and New York up half a cent. Forward silver prices also rose. However, after large deals were made at the closing, prices remained firm because the United States was buying at a premium of 0.0625. Exchange rates fluctuated. London spot gold rose six pence. A Reuters dispatch from Guangdong stated that the provincial committee's proposal for the government to manage exchange rates and revise the ban on silver exports had little impact. Over-the-counter pre-market trading opened, retreated to 67 yuan, and then further retreated to 63.4 yuan. The Central Bank posted exchange rates, with both British and American rates unchanged. Customs gold units rose six yuan. The standard gold price was 918.5 yuan. Short covering was quite active and the market was slightly stable. After the opening, Chinese merchants rushed to sell, and the domestic exchange market hardened. Large players were eager to unload, and prices fell after rising. However, there was still short covering after the fall, and banks also bought on the cheap. But as HSBC also posted higher rates, the market hesitated and was uncertain. Although sentiment was weak, there were many buyers who were willing to buy on the cheap, so the Central Bank and HSBC continued to raise foreign exchange rates, making it easy to pull them up. After entering the market, transactions gradually became more ordinary, and the overall trend became hesitant. Although banks had buying appetite, the domestic market was always ordinary, so the rise lacked momentum. The morning close was slightly weak. In the afternoon, the spread market was tentatively conducted, with the bullish side still posting 1-2 yuan. The market was still weak in the upper market, but the 60 yuan mark was always difficult to approach. After the opening, large players came to cover shorts, and banks also tried hard to buy in, and the market rose. Indian silver initially reported a rise of four annas, and then went into a sideways trend, but was soon pulled up again. At this time, there were very few transactions, and the Indian silver returned to one anna. The market state was mediocre. Finally, prices settled slightly after some selling at the high, but the market was slightly weak after the close. The overall market situation for the day was very ordinary, and transactions were also ordinary. At 3:00 PM today, the April rollover trade will officially begin. After the decline in the yarn market, it has rebounded again. As for the marked yarn for this month, competition between the bulls and bears is fierce. Mou Kee's short positions and Yu Da's long positions are both holding steady, making future changes difficult to predict.

A Sudden Surge in Buying in the Afternoon Market for Gold Chicken

The marked yarn market opened with each month showing stagnation, as both bulls and bears adopted a wait-and-see attitude. Near and far months were down by 2, 3, and 4 jiao. Later, it was heard that spot yarn transactions were still good, resulting in a gain of 2 and 6 jiao for the near months and 3 jiao for the far months.
