Free Talk

From Chivalric Romances to Don Quixote

— Meng Jia

As a pioneer in expressing the themes of chivalric romances, there was the medieval chivalric poetry, including various forms of knightly lyrical poems. The feudal aristocracy, who were the rulers of the Middle Ages, reflected their spirit in the literature of that era. Consequently, chivalric poems, songs of military achievements and martial valor, and lyrical poems reflecting the knightly spirit of courtly love became a major trend in medieval European literature. The protagonists of these works were often nothing more than loyal servants of the country and religion, feeling that they "should endure hardship, cold, and deprivation for the sake of their monarch, without sparing their own flesh and blood," feeling that "food and sweet sleep cannot comfort their hearts like the call to advance to the battlefield," "using special political poems to protect the monarch's rights and threaten or ridicule his enemies," and using love poems to praise the feudal lord's wife, praising her beauty and noble virtues, and expressing the feelings of loyal subjects and knights.

By the 13th century, the feudal structure based on natural economy was gradually eroded and declined by the emerging economy—commercial capitalism. Consequently, the narrative poems (songs) and lyrical poems (love poems), which were the main content of literature during the flourishing period of feudalism, were gradually replaced by prose novels permeated with a strong urban atmosphere. By the 14th century, when bourgeois culture was established in Italy, the medieval poetic forms and styles, the abundant and clear poems that supported and admired the feudal system, and the elements full of asceticism, religious sentiment, miraculous fantasy, and idealistic symbolism, which were artistic expressions of the ideology of the gradually declining knightly and aristocratic classes, such as Dante's poems, had to be replaced by Boccaccio's realistic works, the prose novel "Decameron."

However, with the development of commercial capitalism, the demands of monarchical power arose, and chivalric poetry was revived in Italy. At this time (the 15th century), the new chivalric poems of Italy "arose from the combination of two elements—on one hand, the aristocratic bourgeoisie's taste for chivalric themes, and on the other hand, the lack of artistic completion and the folk ballads full of fairytale-like absurdity and incoherence. These poems idealized knights and their military and amorous adventures, while also incorporating the clumsy techniques and disjointed themes of vulgar folk chivalric poetry." However, what we must pay attention to here is the "parody" of chivalric poetry techniques that occurred simultaneously with this phenomenon. The poem "Morgante" by Pulci, a writer living in Florence, gave a kind of bitter satire and ridicule in the form of "parody" to the feudal system and the revival of chivalric poetry arising from the aristocraticization of the commercial capitalist class. This satirical attitude developed into a unique and complete form in Folengo's poem "Baldus." And the novel by the 16th-century French humanist writer Rabelais, with a solemn and exaggerated approach, a kind of humorous rewriting of chivalric novels popular among commoners and nobles, gave a fierce satire of the feudal knightly system.

The one who achieved the greatest success by utilizing this humorous rewriting of chivalric novels—the technique of "parody"—was Cervantes of 17th-century Spain.

After the 17th century, the Spanish aristocratic class also collapsed due to the rise of the new urban class and its culture. This phenomenon, expressed in literature, on one hand, dealt a fatal blow to the gradually dying knightly class, its culture, and poetry; and on the other hand, "surrounded the knightly posture, which had become a 'shadow of the past,' with a final halo." "Therefore, it is not surprising that the Spanish chivalric novels of this era used the technique of 'parody' to caricature the knightly posture."

Thus, the ugly, old, biased, and skinny "Don Quixote" put on his worn armor, rode his pitiful nag Rocinante, regarded a fat farm girl Dulcinea as a noble lady, and took his squire Sancho Panza, going to do his earth-shattering great deeds.

Although our author used the technique of "parody" to depict the pitiful image of the knight, and permeated it with affectionate ridicule; however, just like Gogol's depiction of the protagonist Akakiy Akakievich in "The Overcoat," his laughter is not cold, but rather melancholy. In the depths of that ridicule, we can taste a kind of almost loving flavor. After making people laugh, he took away a heavy heart, a true melancholy. Cervantes "on one hand, buried the world of knights and knightly literature with ridicule (since 'Mr. Quixote' appeared, Spain has no longer had chivalric novels.) At the same time he was surrounding the head of his own 'knight of the sorrowful countenance' with the shining halo of poetry," this duality expressed in "Mr. Quixote" is also a reflection of Cervantes' ideology as a member of the Spanish petty bourgeoisie who was disintegrating with the decline of the feudal system and the arrival of urban capitalist culture: he clearly understood the collapse and death of the knightly system, thus clearly depicting this "shadow of the past," but also permeated his pen with a lingering emotion, a fallen person's sentimentality for the past; he depicted Quixote as a clownish figure that makes people laugh, while also depicting him as an idealist, a person who is dissatisfied with the existing society (in Lunacharsky's "The Liberated Don Quixote," this quality, which is rich in modern significance, is particularly emphasized.) His ridicule of Quixote, this pitiful knight, can be said to be ridicule dissolved in love, a kind of "laughter with tears."

In the analysis of Quixote's squire Sancho Panza, Friche also similarly emphasizes his duality. Although Sancho Panza seems to be written as a deceitful and cunning character, in reality, this is precisely a typical representation of the materialism of the peasants, which is opposed to the idealism of the aristocrats. In Lunacharsky's "The Liberated Don Quixote," this contrast becomes even more powerful and obvious.

As Friche said: "The commoners have replaced the aristocrats!"

Smoke

— Chi Xia

Lately, my mood often easily slips into boredom. Casually picking up a cigarette to smoke, I feel that my life is as fleeting as that smoke.

"Smoke! Smoke! Everything is a layer of smoke!" Those who have read Turgenev's "Smoke" must remember these words spoken by the protagonist Litvinov!

Unfortunately, I was born and grew up in this hopeless environment. If I didn't have a soul, I could have lived through this era comfortably. However, for those who are slightly sensitive, it's not the same. Nothing can be done, everything can make you feel troubled, everything is like smoke and mist, fleeting like smoke!

Reality is too ugly, which makes those who should have ideals feel as disappointed as smoke. Just like the protagonist Litvinov in the novel "Smoke," although he grew up in a bad environment at first, he still held a glimmer of hope in his heart. However, since he returned home, his father died, and in the old aristocratic mansion, he was left alone. His mood fell into depression, without hope, without passion, and without money. He began land reclamation work. Everyone knows that land reclamation is an impossible dream. His final efforts were shattered, and he fell into nothingness. A year passed, then another year. The third year began, and the great ideal gradually turned into the ugliness of reality. Whether bright or dark, it now bears a gray face that cannot be concealed.

How much does this resemble our current state! It is a living portrayal. Smoke, everything can be represented by smoke! At first, it is very thick, gradually fading, like playing a ridiculous game, gradually lengthening, gradually disappearing. The original mist is lost, the fake mask changes into the true original form, using the mist of smoke to deceive people, to deceive oneself, but this deception is not long-lasting. The result of deception will make you fall into pain, a kind of despairing sorrow, mixed with a false and empty situation.

When smoking, it is easy to have such thoughts. Not smoking? It's also impossible, because in this era, only smoke can comfort oneself and be used to kill painful time!

Dragon Lanterns and Horse Lanterns

— Tang Xiru

I remember when I was a child, once the fifth day of the Lunar New Year had passed, I would look forward to the Lantern Festival, always happily singing:

"The fifteenth of the first month, dragon lanterns and horse lanterns come to see."

When I was a child, I didn't understand anything, I only knew about the excitement. At that time, when dragon lanterns or horse lanterns came, people would set off firecrackers to welcome them. Wealthy families would also join in the fun and set off many flower tubes, moon cannons, nine dragons, and so on.

At that time, the wallets of the people in the countryside seemed to be more full than they are now. They had spare money to play with these many things. The government also seemed to be accommodating the people's feelings and not interfering in their leisure activities. Therefore, the strong and healthy young farmers, on the last days of their only rest and entertainment of the year, would have as much fun as possible.

The sound of gongs and drums grew closer. Then the children of each family would sneak out of the house and rush to where the sound was coming from. Children are always enthusiastic supporters of games. Then the men would come out, followed by the women, and the elderly.

Thinking about it now, dragon lanterns and horse lanterns are actually very monotonous and very tasteless. The gongs and drums always play the same tune. The marching style of the horse lanterns is always the scissors-like movement. The dragon lanterns are also just turning east and west, the dragon's head passing under the dragon's feet, or making a rolling posture on the ground. The movements are really as simple as can be! And so simple as to make people disgusted! But the people in the countryside were crazy! The people in the town were also crazy! Young and old all ran out to watch and admire like crazy! Why? In a word, they lacked entertainment too much on weekdays! Like a person who is starving, as long as they have something to eat, they no longer have any choice about the food!

Moreover, they knew that there was never anything better than this!

Dropping dragon lanterns and horse lanterns is not only for one's own entertainment and to entertain others. They also have other purposes.

Those who play these many things are mostly young farmers. They have the physical strength of oxen. Sometimes they may be exhausted by excessively busy work. But to teach them to do nothing at all for more than ten days, just to rest, they can't get used to it. They can't get used to a lazy life. They like labor. Let those elderly fathers and elders smoke yellow tobacco, play cards, and hold teapots to chat idly. They like to do strenuous, sweaty work. That kind of work is fun!

Dropping these lanterns not only requires strength, but also requires courage. This is a risky move that everyone in the countryside knows. If the lanterns from one village are dropped into another village, the men from the other village can have sufficient reasons, or rather, no reason at all, to provoke them, fight, and tear the lanterns apart! So if you want to play this kind of provocative game, it's not enough to know some martial arts, you also have to have the courage to hit people or be hit, because it's not uncommon for the result to be serious injury or death.

Perhaps you will ask: Why fight? The reason is very simple. It's that everyone admits that those who play these kinds of lanterns are all heroes in the eyes of the villagers, and at the same time, no one admires who is more heroic than whom.

Playing dragon lanterns and horse lanterns, in addition to venting that excess energy, also contains an element of venting sexual desire. Especially the horse lanterns. In the horse lanterns, there is one dressed as a "slutty horse" and one dressed as a "matchmaker." This horse always follows her, making many bold expressions. And she deliberately makes many coy and laughable gestures. Attracting the men to laugh loudly, and the women to scold softly. But everyone likes to watch that kind of action that "civilized people" despise.

There is also a legend about dragon lanterns. It is said that when it is dropped, if a woman who has not been able to conceive for a long time can bare her lower body, cover it with a bamboo cloth skirt, and then grab a handful of grain and quietly sprinkle it on the dragon's head, she will be able to conceive within that year. However, the one who suffers is the person who drops the dragon's head. If he doesn't notice it immediately and lets the woman give him a reward, he will get seriously ill or even die within a year. It seems that dragon lanterns have a great use in helping fertility. (End)

War Jottings (II)

— By Tokunaga Sunao, translated by Ye Yin

"Can one 'go' of support grain feed us to survive!"

Upon seeing the small bag of rice sent two or three times a month from the district chief as support grain for the bereaved families of soldiers who had gone to war, the mother always threw it aside in anger, as if she had been deceived by someone. Every day, she carried huge baskets on a shoulder pole to the barracks of the 23rd Regiment to carry leftover food. Every day, she bought the soldiers' leftovers, or the rice burnt at the bottom of the pot, and the leftover soup, etc., by bidding for a certain amount of money. And, she called the equally poor landladies in the neighborhood and distributed or sold those things to them.

Therefore, since the father went to war, newly cooked rice had hardly been eaten even once; but, in any case, even if it was leftover rice that had been steamed three or four times, we managed to get through the days without feeling hungry.

The second year, I was already seven years old and entered elementary school. At school, whether during games or doing anything, the teachers taught us to sing military songs.

Only costs one 'wen' a month,

Twelve thousand eight hundred tons,

Heard that it's unmatched in the world,

Called Ameuca Boy

I don't remember very clearly; it was probably these kinds of lines. I still remember the tune of the song. From the first grade onwards, we were charged one copper coin each month for the construction of naval warships.

This song was indeed a celebratory song for the construction of a large Japanese warship, unprecedented in the Russo-Japanese War.

That female teacher named Tsuda, protruding her huge, nearly pregnant belly, raised her feet, waved her hands, and used these games and songs to teach us. We formed a circle around the teacher, and during the singing and dancing, the teacher taught us that war was simply extremely noble, and that it was more inferior than being disabled to be born as a human being and not go to war?

In my pure childish heart, I felt that my father fighting outside was a very praiseworthy thing; and, I had a lot of face among my playmates.

One morning, after paying the highest respects to the Emperor's image in the schoolyard, the principal called the students whose fathers were soldiers who had gone to war to the podium to express their feelings. Needless to say, elementary school students would not express such feelings etc. in front of everyone; the head teachers had us memorize the phrases to say the day before. I, a first-grade student, was the second to be called to the podium by the principal.

I was very flustered; I just tried my best to say the phrases that I had memorized by rote in a loud voice.

"My father is a transportation soldier of the 6th Battalion of the Army Transport Corps, Transport Soldier of the Transport Corps, Tokunaga Isokichi, ——"

As soon as I said this, the older children in the upper grades giggled. I was inexplicably confused and felt very embarrassed and couldn't speak. The principal glared at everyone and said:

"No laughing!"

The Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talk

Dreadful Elementary School Students with Lung Disease

— Xing An

This is indeed an extremely serious problem that cannot be ignored! According to the previous tuberculosis test conducted by this city on elementary school students, five schools including Bede, Xicheng, He'an, Danhua, and Songxue participated. The results of the test showed that among the students tested in the five schools, a total of 2,916 students, 2,137 were infected, 739 were not infected, and the reactions of 40 were unknown. Looking at the statistics after the test, the infected reached more than 70 percent. Just testing over 2,000 elementary school students in five schools has yielded such an alarming number. If all the municipal elementary schools in Shanghai were to conduct the test, the number would be even more impressive. So many elementary school students in our country suffer from lung disease. Can we still ignore this problem? Isn't it extremely serious?

Lung disease is a very terrible disease, which can kill one person in a small case, and destroy a nation in a large case. Therefore, all countries in the world pay great attention to this disease. They are doing their best to study the methods of prevention, treatment, and eradication. Their view of lung disease is no different from treating a demon, staying away from it for fear of being too close, and eliminating it for fear of not being far enough. Because once this disease is allowed to spread and spread, the life of the individual and the root of the nation are in danger of falling into an unimaginable desperate situation!

Only we Chinese people have always been indifferent to various aspects of hygiene. And the symptoms of lung disease have become an extremely common phenomenon. If a detailed investigation and examination is made of the number of Chinese people who have contracted lung disease, and statistics are compiled, I am afraid that the number will also surprise people, or even more than 70 percent!

The cause of lung disease can be traced to two sources. One is congenital, inherited from parents who have lung disease. The other is acquired, transmitted by lung disease from those nearby. Chinese people have always been very free about marriage, and have never been interfered with by the government. Therefore, even men and women with lung disease can get married casually. As a result, the children born to Chinese people often have a hereditary predisposition to lung disease. This is why there are so many people with lung disease in our country. As for the fact that Chinese people do not pay attention to hygiene and spit everywhere, this is also one of the reasons for the increase in lung disease.

From this point of view, the prevention of lung disease should be rescued from two aspects. For the symptomatic method, the government should set up more lung disease treatment centers in various places, and persuade the people to pay full attention to hygiene, and prohibit people from spitting everywhere. For the fundamental method, the government should restrict people's marriage. All men and women who want to get married must be examined by a doctor and hold a health certificate before they can marry together. If they have lung disease, they should be strictly prohibited from marrying. This method has been implemented in foreign countries for a long time, and the effect is very significant. Our country should take it as a model as soon as possible.

For the elementary school students who have been examined this time, it is heard that the Bureau of Education has notified the families of students who have been injected and have a lung disease reaction to quickly seek treatment on their own, and re-examine them after a considerable period of time, limiting the admonishment to three times. If they still ignore it, they will be ordered to withdraw from school. On the one hand, the two bureaus of Health and Education, for the future of the health of all the children in the city, decided to set up a children's sanatorium in the municipal hospital which is under construction. This approach is urgent. However, we hope even more that the education and health authorities will conduct another tuberculosis test in all schools in Shanghai in the near future in order to engage in thorough prevention. Furthermore, we ask the government authorities to pay attention to the spread of lung disease, to quickly consider fundamental methods of eradication, and that the harm of lung disease is very fierce. I sincerely hope that the people of our country will pay attention to defense and prevent it from spreading, so as not to become a disaster for the people of our country!

It Is Better to Return Home

— Bu Yang

(The cuckoo is also known as the Zi Gui bird, its cries are utterly mournful, as if saying it is better to return home, it is better to return home.)

Time flies by on the calendar, life churns in a whirlpool, listen! It is the season for cuckoo cries again.

What touching melodies of homesickness! Travelers.

My heart is deeply moved; yes, it tells me: it is time to go home.

I received a letter from Ling saying: "Qingming is approaching, wild grasses have grown all over your father's grave, you should come back to sweep and pay respects. Your mother and I miss you so much! And Yi'er, whom you haven't seen for half a year, can now call 'Daddy' at your photo. Come back soon! Come and accept your son's call."

Like the cuckoo's cry, my heart is deeply moved. Yes, I need to go back.

My hometown, which I haven't seen for half a year! Now I am preparing to throw myself back into your embrace.

I remember when I left, it was autumn, you were so melancholic, like Ling's face when saying goodbye, how sad it made people! Now I'm coming back soon, surely you will change your attire to welcome me.

So I close my eyes and think—the fields I haven't seen for half a year are covered with a carpet of oily green, the branches I haven't seen for half a year are draped in verdant coats, the stream I haven't seen for half a year is limpid and softly manipulated by the March spring breeze at will, here you can still see two or three fat white geese comfortably splashing in the water, pairs of swallows lightly skimming over the water to glimpse their own lovely shadows, and patches of clouds leisurely racing across the bottom of the water... Yes, it's not like when I left, it's like Ling's face when she knows I'm coming home: full of youthful smiles.

I am still so familiar with the spring in my hometown, but I wonder if my hometown in the spring still recognizes me? That person is not like before, the childishness of past years, like the fallen leaves in autumn, has been stripped away by the storms of reality, leaving only: a husk-like body and an ash-like soul.

Perhaps my hometown will be unfamiliar with me? But I must come back, it is the first Qingming after my father's death! I must stand before his old tomb and offer my sincere respect, I must tell him about my experiences after our eternal farewell, I must carefully examine the surrounding grasses.

My mother after my father's death is in pain, she has placed all her hope on her son. She cares about her son's safety even more than she cares about her own, and she is extremely unwilling for her son to know about occasional minor illnesses, oh great maternal love! I haven't experienced it for half a year. How much new white hair has been added to her head? How much new wrinkles have been added to her forehead? I must return and lean in her arms like when I was young, tell her that I am doing well outside, tell her not to worry, and then look up and see a kind smile spread across her kind face.

Ling has become much haggard since having a child, and because of the environment, I can't hire a nanny for her. So she has to do everything herself regarding the child, and the pair of hands that have been dyed rough by labor truly make me unable to bear to hold them. For whom? I can only blame myself. I shouldn't let her taste the bitterness of separation again, I must go back.

Sitting face to face with Ling, let Yi'er, who has just learned to walk, stagger from here to there. Suddenly, he cries because he feels unfamiliar, so Ling picks him up and says: "This is Daddy, isn't he just like this picture?" Saying this, she points to the photo hanging on the wall.

A pair of small, dark, and round eyes look at the wall, look at me, and then look at Ling, his mother, he laughs, so innocently.

"Daddy," Ling calls out.

"Daddy," Yi'er imitates.

The people of my hometown are all waving to me] I must go back.

I take a leave form from the manager's office to fill out, and then tidy up the few books I have.

(Cuckoo, don't cry! I am listening to you.)

Overnight Stay on the River

— Hua Zhi

The days in winter are very short, and our small boat was still drifting on the wide river, and it was already the time for crows to return to their nests. From morning until now, although I forgot to bring a watch when I set off in a hurry, I had been sitting with my knees bent for so long that my legs had gone from aching to numb. There was a pack of leftover cigarettes in my pocket, and even the lining paper was folded into small boats, which were placed dozens of feet behind me. Feeling a kind of disappointment after fatigue, we yawned in unison and stretched our legs, which were about to detach from ourselves, but the boat suddenly tilted, and the elderly couple almost rushed from the bow into the center of the river.

"Sir, this is not a game!" The old man pulled the pole out of the river bottom, bent over, and faced the door of the boat and said.

"Where will we stay tonight?" This was the question that I was concerned about.

"There's probably a small town ahead, but it's against the wind and against the current, and we can't muster any strength to row there. Those of you sitting in the cabin don't know the hardship of the boatmen. We almost fell into the center of the river just now, and who would fish us out in the dark?" As he spoke, he vigorously poled towards the center of the river.

I poked my head out from the cabin door, and the river stretched windingly forward, as if there would never be a stop. On both banks of the fields, the evening wind stirred, and it was impossible to distinguish between people and grass. A collapsed oxcart shed gradually moved behind us. Focusing my eyes on the farthest distance, I didn't see any trace of the so-called small town. Instead, I received the boatman's complaint, and I felt angry in my heart.

"What's the name of that town?"

"It seems—I've forgotten. Ask a passerby to see."

I couldn't help but curse "Damn it" in my heart. After sitting on the boat for a whole day, I hadn't seen a single person except for seeing a piece of otter skin dog napping under the sun when I first got on the boat. Now he was talking so easily? I was too lazy to argue with him, so I shrank back into the cabin.

In a moment, it was pitch black. They made their home on the water, and they didn't mind tying the boat tightly to the shore and staying overnight in this wilderness. But could you disagree? We couldn't lift the pole, we couldn't row the oars, and besides, it was pitch black in all directions.

The couple climbed to the stern, skillfully carried the cooking utensils to the shore, gathered some wild firewood, and asked us if we wanted to eat their Xian rice. They skillfully started a fire. That fellow Li Ma had been sulking the whole time, but now his stomach probably couldn't hold out any longer, and he threw all the terror to the back of his mind and climbed ashore.

I ate a very comfortable meal. This means that I could stretch my arms and legs at this time of day, and my stomach was empty, so the rice tasted unexpectedly sweet. However, the problem came next: how could this small boat accommodate so many passengers? Although the old couple spread out a tattered quilt and slept on the bow, we still slept with our knees bent as before.

Everyone was extremely tired. The two boatmen who had been working for a whole day naturally fell asleep as soon as their heads hit the pillows. We couldn't close our eyes the whole time. All the terrors were subconsciously fighting in our minds. Hearing the distant barking of dogs, it seemed that misfortune was about to befall us immediately. This was an era of turmoil!

Worrying and guarding, I didn't fall asleep peacefully until the next day when the boat set sail; in reality, I could no longer endure the torture of exhaustion.

Festival Day

— Si Lang

"××! Please come out quickly to watch the lion dance!" The landlord's child was shouting loudly. At first, I thought she was teasing me. Where did the lion come from? I pretended not to hear and ignored her, but after a while, the landlord's wife also came to my room to ask: "The lion dance is so good, why don't you watch it?" I then believed that there really was such a thing, but I still didn't understand what the lion dance was all about. Later, after the landlord's wife explained it to me, I learned that this was a scene from a Japanese festival day. It is said that on this festival day, in addition to the lion dancers going to the door of every house to perform a dance, which is considered a blessing; a platform is also set up in the shrine to perform plays. It was really lively! So I went to the shrine with the landlord's child.

It was a good day, a clear sky, with the sun hanging in the sky, the sun shining on the earth, and all living things were flourishing because of it. The little birds on the branches were also rejoicing because of it, singing natural songs. It was truly a season when spring had arrived in the world! The landlord's child and I came out of the house and ran over a small hill, because the shrine was on the other side of the hill. A stone frame that seemed to be made up of two crosses joined together was considered the first gate of the shrine. On top of it were hung some things like mirrors and porcelain used to ward off evil spirits in Chinese temples. Both sides were full of pine and cypress trees, a verdant green. In the middle was a stone staircase, and we rushed up the stairs, passing through several stone frame gates before reaching the square in front of the shrine. In addition to a stage for performing plays, there were also some stalls selling food and toys on the square. Many children were gathered there, and some were dressed in brand-new clothes like the children in Chinese villages when watching the parade of gods. Because the play on the stage had not yet started, we went into the shrine to take a look for a while. All the settings were similar to those in China, but they were smaller and more elegant than ordinary Chinese temples. Especially the flocks of pigeons that hopped around freely there, just like the quiet and poetic atmosphere of a Greek church. The play on the stage began, and we stood there for half a day, and only saw a drummer and a flute player squatting in a corner of the stage playing music. The tune was old and solemn. The setting on the stage was very simple, with two door curtains hanging, a low table placed, a bowl of clear water placed on top, and also two staffs. A person wearing an old man's mask, wearing ancient clothes, and holding a court tablet in his hand, kept kneeling to the four directions, making various dance-like postures according to the old and solemn music. There was no new or interesting play to watch. Ah! This is the so-called "Festival Day" in Japan.

Page 21

Peanut Boat

—

Whenever I peel a peanut in my hand, I will inevitably think of the story of the peanut boat: especially the old man with the silver beard on a peanut boat, and a little girl with double buns, I still remember them at all times.

All the people on the peanut boats are from Jiangbei. Normally, these boats do not come here. Their profession, in addition to selling peanuts, is usually fishing or ferrying. A small boat is considered a home, and all the living and eating are done here. Life only relies on such a broken small boat.

In our hometown, every year in winter, many small boats, loaded with peanuts, are parked in every port in front of and behind the mountains. Every day, they carry a sack of peanuts on their backs and go to various villages and alleys to sell them;

"Long life fruit! Long life fruit for sale"! In this season, you can hear this short and harsh cry on any street or in any alley. This teases a group of children, who pester adults for copper coins to buy long life fruit, and the elders have to spend a few extra copper coins every day.

After they sell out the peanuts, the women go to the mountain mines to hammer stones; the men go to dig red mud, or work as small laborers in lime kilns. When the lunar new year comes, their whole family, old and young, carry bamboo baskets on their arms, or cloth bags on their shoulders, and go from house to house to beg for cakes, perform lion dances, and sing the money tree song. They can do everything. Because the villagers like to hear good words at the beginning of the new year, and do not want to be cursed, so as long as they can speak and sing, and add some auspicious words of "getting rich and blessed," then a piece of cake or two pieces of dumplings will not disappoint them. This is indeed a very good speculative career for them. After going out and peddling for a day, each person can get at least fifteen or sixteen catties of cakes and dumplings.

I remember in the early winter of a certain year, a peanut boat was also parked in the narrow port in front of our door. That boat was so dilapidated that it was almost about to sink. There were only two people on the boat, an old man in his fifties, and a little girl about twelve or thirteen years old. Like other peanut boats, they carried peanuts out to sell during the day and returned to sleep on the boat at night. However, every day when the old man went out to sell peanuts, he always left the little girl with double buns in the boat to guard it.

The boat had been parked in front of our door for many days, and I naturally gradually became acquainted with the little girl on the boat: and became friends with her, mixing together every day. I learned that her name was Xiao Xizi; she was the old man's granddaughter. As for her parents, she heard that they had died, she only knew that they had died in the water, but she didn't know in which year, which place, or how they died. However, her grandfather didn't let her know either.

As long as the old man was not there, I would run to the boat to play with her, and Xiao Xizi often secretly gave me many peanuts. But as soon as the old man came back, I would slip away, and Xiao Xizi would also run back to the cabin as if she were a mouse seeing a cat. It wasn't that the old man was fierce, he had never scolded us, he was also a kind old man, but children seemed to be a little afraid of adults.

In January of the following year, they also opened up like other peanut boats, and then took away my companion—the lovely Xiao Xizi! At this time, I felt infinite disappointment and loneliness, as if I had lost a heart.

That winter, the peanut boat came again as usual, but it didn't bring back my companion. Later, I went to ask the old man, and he only coldly replied: "She is dead"!

In the third year, at this time in the peanut season, I didn't see the old man's broken boat anymore, and another peanut boat had replaced it in the port in front of our door.

Homesick Patient

— Jing Yao

On our ship, there is an old fellow who everyone calls crazy. The second day I came to this ship, people told me:

"That old drunkard is crazy."

Yes, he does love to drink a bit. There's always a wine bottle slanting in his pocket. His face is always so red. Whenever he does something, he takes the wine bottle out of his pocket, tilts his head, puts the mouth of the bottle to his lips, and watches his dry, wrinkled arms with blue veins bulging. A gurgling sound comes from his throat. A few big gulps of wine, and it's gone into his belly. Immediately, his scattered eyes have more light, and he has more energy to do things. It's like he can't live without drinking.

Saying he's crazy, well, that's not necessarily true. Looking at his face under his white hair, he always looks locked in gloom. He doesn't like to talk, and no one talks to him. He's often looking at the distant sea in solitude. It's as if there's something he's longing for in the distant sea. Maybe his temper is a bit strange? Crazy? I think that's a rumor about him.

"Don't make trouble! He's such an old man."

"It's true! Don't you believe it?" The partner who told me this got agitated by my words and started arguing.

"I didn't believe it like you did before, but then I found out. Don't believe it? Let's try it." He pulled me to stand in front of the old fellow on the deck.

"Hey! Old drunkard..."

He was staring at the distant sea in a trance, his hands on the ship's railing, his whole body leaning slightly forward. Looking at his pale green, thin face from the side, he looked so indifferent, not at all… Looking at his solemn, gloomy expression, it's really impossible to guess what's hidden in his aging body, in that aging heart. What is he thinking? What is he longing for?

"Hey! Old drunkard! Is the wine you're drinking today good?"

"Wine? Is this even wine? The water in the Hetao area in our hometown is stronger than this." The old fellow's words were just as indifferent. He didn't turn his head away from gazing at the distant sea, he just shrugged his shoulders.

"So, when are you going home?" My partner winks at me.

"Go home?" Those words seemed to stab him in his wound, and he turns around to retort. His eyes are burning with red threads, as if they are on fire. His face is gradually turning pale.

"Dreaming of going home! Go home? The train isn't free. If it were ten years ago, I'd crawl back; but now my legs are old! Old!" As he said this, the sadness of old age floats up, like the dusk on the sea.

"I've wanted to go home for so many years. I can only dream about it. You see this wine bottle, it's been with me all these years, I rely on it to dream, as soon as I drink wine, I'm home. Haha, old friend!" He takes out his wine bottle again.

The old fellow puts the wine bottle to his mouth, gurgling as he drinks, mumbling as he goes:

"I have a home, and it's so good! There are mountains, there is water, there are herds of sheep, there is bleached snow, there are big pine trees, there are purple mountain grapes, there is better wine than this, there is..."

I couldn't help but ask:

"Where is your home?"

"My home? My home is right there!" He points to the sea shrouded in twilight with his wine bottle.

In that distant sea, there are a few seabirds flying. The infinitely distant distance, dyed with dusk, faintly has a few sails appearing and disappearing.

On the Banks of the Irrawaddy River

— Hua Mu

Except for two seasons, the gentle breeze from the Irrawaddy River will blow through the coconut groves. The days pass slowly under the scorching sun throughout the year. During a languid midnight, wrapped in a light and smooth Changjiang Man cloth, lying on a bamboo-mat-covered bed, listening leisurely to the wind chimes on the golden pagoda, scattering a lonely melody; the coconut groves send out the songs of Burmese women, gently harmonizing with the low-pitched steelpan piano. The original lively and unrestrained style of the South Island penetrates the deep and helpless sorrow of a lost country. The melody drags the tail of the sound for a long time, slowly fading away in the lonely wind chimes, fading away. What remains is a lazy and verdant coconut grove, with squirrels chirping and jumping comically on the large leaves of the coconut trees. A kind of indescribable fatigue lightly floats through my heart. This midnight on the equator makes me forget the scorching sun and the bitterness of wandering in a foreign land.

In the distance, crows cry mournfully. It is the time when the market disperses, and the Burmese have spent another day quietly.

Stepping out of the door, the scorching wind blows over from the river. My head is a little dizzy. The coconut tree leaves shield the sun above my head, and when the river breeze gently blows through the leaves, fragmented sunlight is filtered down onto the green grass. In front of me, the blue Irrawaddy River quietly ripples and flows eastward. Looking far away, the coconut groves on the opposite bank also quietly and verdantly lean against the solemn and silent green peaks, appearing as a lush green. The high sky is endlessly blue, without a single cloud. Sometimes, a few eagles will fly over, circling with a free and proud posture. Looking along the river, the distant mountain scenery and green shadows vaguely cut off the ribbon-like river flow. At this time, a sampan leisurely descends from the upper reaches, its white sails appearing and disappearing through the shadows of the coconut tree leaves as it flows downstream. The Burmese boatmen on the boat, with their bare, dark backs, look up blankly at the green shade on the shore, perhaps envying the coolness of the coconut trees and weary of the painful life on the water. When the white sails vaguely disappear into the green shadows, like a gypsy's light sorrow, it bites at my heart, causing me to sigh leisurely.

At the edge of the coconut grove, there is a flat dirt road that stretches straight to the southern fields. Looking along the dirt road, a golden and abundant rice field indicates that it is the harvest season. At this time, a cart creaks and staggers past. The Burmese women inside the cart emit a frivolous laughter, calling out: "Deru, Deru." —Chinese—…

The sound of the oxcart gradually fades away, fades away. Suddenly, with a "honk" sound, the momentary silence is broken, and a steamship with the British flag flies away across the river. The quiet river surface suddenly stirs up restless waves, and white water splashes onto the green grassy bank, hissing and rustling. The thick smoke in the air stretches long at the top of the coconut grove, like a black python coiling there, opening its mouth wide, greedily devouring everything on the banks of the Irrawaddy River!

The river surface gradually calms down. In the distance, mournful crow calls rise again. The wind chimes on the golden pagoda still scatter a lonely melody. The days pass slowly under the scorching sun throughout the year, and now it is the harvest season again. However, decades of insatiable exploitation have forced the Burmese to hide in the coconut groves, supporting their work-worn bodies and minds, and watching the black python circling over the Irrawaddy River, singing the deep and helpless song of a lost country.

Jiang Ruting and Zhu Jiesheng: Broken Golden Fan

China (1140) 9:00 PM to 9:45 PM

Opening "National Goods"

This year we happily celebrate the National Goods Year, when countrymen love their country above all else.华洋雜處春申地, 商埠繁華孰並肩, Every time the lamps are lit, the streets are bustling one after another. The people mostly like foreign goods, causing the country to be weak and the people to be poor, which is truly pitiful. How many leakages are hard to calculate, causing people to sigh as if enduring torture. Therefore, countrymen advocate for Chinese goods, and national goods markets are established everywhere. They frequently use words to promote them. Most hateful are those who like to use Japanese goods, forgetting their grievances and greedily taking advantage of cheap prices. They earn our money to build guns and cannons. Their evil hearts are as poisonous as arsenic. I hope my compatriots will quickly awaken and not be as if drunk or in a dream. If we can resolutely resist, and learn from Goujian's perseverance, we can guarantee that the Japanese invaders will meet their end. Commercial competition is the trend of today, and any style is valuable if it is fresh. We should understand that economic aggression has plagued us for years, more so than tens of thousands of military feats. From now on, do not use foreign goods to avoid leakages to foreign countries. I advise you not to just pay lip service.

Yao Xiao'an and Wang Pingqiu: Qilin Leopard

Sino-Western (1040) 11:00 PM to 12:00 AM

Opening "Wild Goose"

Wild geese shadows fly south across the blue sky. The distant Western Mountains accompany the road's splendor. Yet only the sound vanishes beyond Hengyang with no information. Startled by the cold, the vast water elaborates white clouds. The long sky's wild goose script conveys letters. The early new autumn this year quickly arrives. I sigh for the traveling husband far away. The long journey extends to Yanmen Pass. A beautiful woman suddenly dreams of longing. Boundless sorrow fills her heart. She only thinks of her good man serving in the military. I do not know what day he can return south. A line of intimate geese cry in the sky. I imagine tonight they will rest on the reed shoal. I only see those married pairs of geese. The bridal chamber's red candles light up double brilliance. Brothers all enjoy family happiness. Harmony unites as hands and feet follow along. Therefore, harmony can not be scattered. The solitary leader possesses power. Where have the snow marks and goose tracks gone? Everywhere one hears they are under command. Righteousness surpasses the sky, admired for thousands of years. A feather hopes to return south. Cat tails flower and white waves compete in flight. The sand bar shakes feathers now and again. A bay of green water happily ripples. A sad cry evokes feelings of home. Next year, the autumn wind may arrive again. I happily see the returning wild geese.

Classical Chinese Prose

Wang Bingmei: Donglai's Extensive Discussion

Hua Xing (1260) 9:00 AM to 10:00 AM

Duke Yin Asks About the Number of Feathers (Continued)

Since King Cheng used the rites and music of the Son of Heaven to worship the Duke of Zhou, it has been hundreds of years to Duke Yin. With the virtue of King Cheng, he bestowed them, and with the virtue of Bo Qin, he received them. The world did not know that it was wrong. Later, they were used in the temples of the dukes, and the country did not know that it was wrong either. Duke Yin was born hundreds of years later and was the only one who could doubt the mistakes of hundreds of years. However, he was uneasy and asked about it. His natural talent was high. Zhong Zhong told him about the proper rites of the former kings, so that the offering of six feathers could be seen again at the banquet of Zhong Zhi. It cannot be said that it was without benefit. However, the question of Duke Yin was not only for the temple of Zhong Zi. It was only because of the temple of Zhong Zi that he raised the question. Zhong Zhong fully explained that the Duke of Zhou created rites and music to bring about peace. The Son of Heaven used eight rows, and the dukes used six rows. This was the music created by the Duke of Zhou. The Duke of Zhou created the number of this music and dance because he wanted to practice it in the world and pass it on to future generations. The Duke of Zhou wanted to practice it in the world, but his descendants had already disrupted it. He wanted to pass it on to future generations, but he had already violated it after his death. If the Duke of Zhou had known, I know he would not have enjoyed the sacrifices of Lu.

Shen Bao Local Supplement, Movie Special

In the Rumors of "Suicide," Keen Harro's Attachment to This World (Part 2)

— Xue Mei

"Also, I like to wear pajamas the most. Pajamas are my weakness. I always like to wear pajamas when I have a casual meal at a friend's house. If I have a banquet tonight and must wear formal wear, Blanc has already prepared my formal wear and all the small things without me saying a word. But when I want to go to an informal dinner and wear pajamas, she tells me that the pajamas have been sent to the laundry. Of course, I have more than a dozen pairs of pajamas, and they would never all go to the laundry. But Blanc doesn't let me wear pajamas, so I have to wear formal wear.

"Cleaning the room is originally the duty of a male servant, but since Blanc came, she has never let a male servant enter my bedroom, dressing room, and bathroom. She always cleans and wipes herself. My underwear, socks, handkerchiefs, and everything close to my skin, she also refuses to take outside, always washing them herself. Whether I get up early or come home late, she is always by my side. She always refuses to leave before I am asleep. If I invite friends to dine at home, she doesn't go on her holidays. She doesn't trust others to do her job. She can distinguish the good from the bad. When unreliable people come, she always comes in and out of my room, never leaving my side. She can find things to do, walking back and forth, and secretly monitoring that person.

"Also, I am naturally lazy and like to put good things to do today until tomorrow. Blanc often reminds me every morning of what I should do or should reply to a letter. I say, "Okay, I'll do it later." Blanc must wait until the "later" time comes before she will stop. For example, if I promise to return someone's call, and the time comes, if I don't return that person's call, she will connect the phone, making it impossible for me to delay. I don't break my promises to friends, mostly because of Blanc's help. Although I felt she was annoying at the time, I am very grateful to her afterward.

"Blanc has a deep understanding of me. I'm afraid no one understands me more deeply except my mother. She knows all my temperaments, personalities, habits, hobbies, etc. She knows my various faults, laziness, forgetfulness, wastefulness, often not wearing socks, and walking out wearing long pants, putting things to do today until tomorrow. She knows all this, but she still loves me.

"All women, when they are in front of men, always act a little, whether they are fathers, brothers, or husbands. This acting, or unconscious, is always an acting. When they arrive in their private rooms, when they sleep or get up, bathe, or dress, that is their real life, without any acting. At that time, in that place, all the defenses are removed, and all the covers are stripped off. This is the true nature of naked women. What Blanc knows about me is the naked me.

"When I leave this world and go to another world, I also want her to tell people about me like this, and what I want to remember and cherish is all the trivial things I said above, socks, long pants—that kind of loyalty, that kind of care, that kind of love is rarely described in words."

"Strangely enough, last night I was flipping through my scrapbook with newspaper headlines pasted on it, recording my life's deeds. Some were accurate, some were inaccurate, some were praising, some were sarcastic. I thought that if I died, these things would be remembered. What I want to remember and take to another world are just some daily trivialities."

Keen Harro's words are finished. Will she commit suicide? Suicide, suicide, is all because there is nothing to miss in this world. It must be known that suicide is ultimately a sign of cowardice. It is useless to oneself, and people will laugh at it after death, at most gaining some pity. If you don't want to commit suicide, you must be able to understand the love of life, appreciate the beauty of life, and have an attachment to life, like Keen Harro. A person like Keen Harro will never commit suicide. She can appreciate the love and expectations of others for her. She doesn't want to let herself down, others down, or the world down. Even if she is oppressed and tormented by the environment, she will not lightly yield. (End)

Movie Review

Review of "Adventure Girl"

— Hua Lun

Adventure Girl is showing at the Great Shanghai.

After many so-called hero adventure movies, the producer gives us this "Heroine's Adventure". This is aimed at "Go see how women go on adventures" and the "business eye" of people who are tired of watching the previous kind of works. If you make any excessive demands on things produced from this "business eye", it is naturally afraid that it will be difficult to fulfill them.

Here, apart from the lack of a strict structure, the lack of a central story, and only travel, objectively for national aggression and subjectively for self-enrichment adventures, these are not much different from all similar works.

The whole film is said to be made according to the female protagonist's own writings, narrating her adventure experience travelogue. Although there is also Herman Ravmaker, who is said to have directed it, the film is really not brilliant enough, and strictly speaking, it can only be regarded as a dubbed news film or travel record.

With the female protagonist Joan Lowell—that is, the character in the play—and a sailor Su Yi as the center, it is divided into several sections. First, it starts with Joan and the others setting sail, followed by the shipwreck in the howling wind, Su Yi falling into the water, and Joan swimming to save him. The next morning, Joan and others searched a wrecked ship and found a map recording the location of the gems, and decided to find it. However, because the drinking water on the ship was cut off, in the difficulty of thirst, they had to go ashore to duel with poisonous snakes and beasts to obtain drinks. From this scene to their destination, a certain island, they went to the place where the gems were stored with the queen of the natives. Because stealing gems violated the religious sanctity of the natives and the ancestors of the queen, they were captured by the natives and burned alive. While the delicate body was being burned and the natives celebrated their victory, Su Yi rushed to save her, and after experiencing some thrilling pursuits, they escaped onto their own ship and sailed away.

Although the story is not sound enough, it can be regarded as having some plot. If the director could structure it more and use some film art techniques, it would be much better than what is currently being shown.

What is now shown on the screen is full of inconsistencies and clumsiness everywhere: such as the ship's hull and the items in the cabin, most of the wood and iron are old, broken, and unbearable, but the box containing the map is uniquely intact. What the picture tells the audience is obviously only five coconuts were carried back to quench their thirst, but then it is written that the problem of drinking water was completely solved. There is a gun in Su Yi's hand, which has frightened countless wild birds, but in the fight with the queen's chief adjutant and in the many fights where she was desperately chased by the natives, she never fired a shot. How inconsistent is this! As for writing the so-called native empress so mediocre that she looks like a bowing oriental maid, and there are white people in Western clothes mixed in the native group, this is not only untrue, but also completely loses the power of the play. From the queen's helplessness, it is obvious that she is a very untrained temporary actor. In addition, the not-so-beautiful stream scenery and the water flowing in the lush forest are repeated again and again without principle or necessity. When writing about sailing in extreme crisis, one must also start from the heavy cable machine, the anchor cable gradually comes out of the water, the sail rope is untied, and the sails are gradually raised one by one, and then the ship moves. These completely cannot see a trace of so-called editing techniques.

If there are any advantages, it is that the suffering of the lack of water in the ship in the front is deeply and concisely written with scenes of the cat's tongue stretching out, its feet grasping the basin, and the people's exhaustion, etc.

The Stars in "The Night in Young"

— Yun Shui

"The Night in Young", hailed as MGM's greatest musical and dance blockbuster of 1935, is now being released by "Nanjing". This is an artistic work that directly pursues "The Cat and the Fiddle". Only in the handling of the story, the background is turned into a palace, and the male and female protagonists are all brilliant big stars in Hollywood: Ramon Novarro... Ramon is a handsome and good-singing young man that everyone knows. Since he emerged in "Ben-Hur" in the silent film era, he has become a standard handsome man and a hero in the dreams of heterosexuals. Later, he co-starred with Garbo in the famous historical film about the German female spy Mata Hari, translated as "Mata Hari". His most recent work last year was "The Cat and the Fiddle" with Jeanette MacDonald. Of course, his singing talent won him a great victory here again. Ramon is Mexican. He was born in Durango on February 6th. He is rich in the study of drama, and the color of his hair and eyes is especially stimulating for Exotio (this is of course a white people's word). In "The Night in Young", he plays the Duke Paul of that kind.

Evelyn Laye... Evelyn is a famous singer on the British stage. Later, she joined the film and was recruited by MGM to Hollywood. She was born in London on July 10th. She now plays the actress Lise in the film.

We at least have a considerable understanding of the other five big stars. They are Holden, the humorous founder of the ambassador who once played "The Merry Widow". He has also appeared in famous films such as "Diary of a Lost Girl" and "The Passionate Plumber". The audience probably also likes his Zhuang Xie and wonderful art. He is Baron Schleinitz in this film. And that nice guy C. Bugger-Worth is here again. The fat man who plays the waiter is the famous German comedian Hermann Piff. And the one who plays Otto is Henry Stephenson. As for the two actresses, the one who plays Lise's companion Fanny is the exquisite Una Merkel. The one who plays the Laifei woman is the graceful Rosaline Russell.

Ramon Novarro and Evelyn Laye in "The Night in Young", MGM's greatest song and dance palace musical structure of this year—now showing in Nanjing.

Star Anecdotes

(1) "Night-Blooming Jasmine Has Already" completed one-third, and director Cheng Bugao is now actively engaged in the dubbing work of the film.

(2) "Nostalgia" filmed a scene at an orphanage yesterday, with as many as two or three hundred child actors.

(3) In "When the Flowers Fall", there is a great trench set, which is now being built in a hurry. In the past few days, the Mingxing outdoor studio has been covered with wire mesh and sandbags. After this scene is finished, "When the Flowers Fall" will be completed.

Movie Novel

Anecdotes of Wellington (The Iron Duke) (8)

— Xin Zhi

Kitty said, "Don't embarrass him. The mistake is not only on him." Wellington smiled and walked out. Francis's husband was a tall, thin man, very young. He had taken off his coat, but he was still wearing his hat and his face was full of anger. Wellington politely asked him to sit down, but he didn't sit. Wellington smiled and said, "Your wife's friendship is a great honor. Please sit down." The man said angrily, "Of course, I can't listen to you alone."

Wellington said, "I am a soldier, and I am willing to be a gentleman. Of course, you must also listen to your wife." The man said sharply, "You ordered everyone to stay in Brussels and wrote a letter asking my wife to leave. What's the reason?" Wellington said, "To let her return to London to welcome you back." The man asked again, "Why didn't she?"

Wellington was about to stammer and couldn't explain why, when suddenly Francis walked in and shouted, "Weber, I'll tell you..." Her face was pale and her lips were slightly trembling. She continued, "I heard there was a war there, and I want to take a look. When Napoleon was defeated, I was near Waterloo. I had the opportunity to see Wellington fight. Don't you want me to see it?" Her husband scolded angrily, "What does this have to do with Paris?" Francis said, "Then you say I love the Duke of Wellington? That's right, I love him, but not in the way we understand it... You can also say it is admiration and respect, because one day in the future, history will record: he is the only great man, loyal minister, and warrior..."

"She said, sobbing. She choked and said, "But, Weber, I still love you." She fell into her husband's arms. The anger on her husband's face also disappeared instantly. He kissed her fiercely. Wellington watched, smiled, bowed, and withdrew.

Kitty was waiting for him in the hall. She said, "Aser, I want to keep Webster here for dinner. Is that okay?" Wellington smiled and said, "Very good, who wants him to let Francis sit on my right! You, sit opposite me." Kitty asked again, "Can you stay at home for a few more days this time?" Wellington said, "I have to go back to Paris first and arrange for the Duchess of Anoel. I can tell you the details of this disaster now. This is the conspiracy of that woman. She spent money and bribed an unscrupulous London newspaper reporter to write this piece of news for her. She had no other way, so she used this last despicable method." Kitty said, "That's also very pitiful."

In the palace in Paris, Louis was sitting on the real throne as usual. His foolish face still showed a look of anxiety. Outside the palace gate, there was a clamor. A group of angry people approached the palace gate. Their shouts shook the sky, getting louder and louder. Louis panicked and said, "The crowd is getting bigger and bigger. Why doesn't anyone go to suppress them?" The Duchess of Anoel stood beside Louis, silent. Her face was pale and her heart was full of fear. Louis said again, "Why did you insist on me signing the death sentence of General Nan Yi? According to my idea, I was not willing to do that, but now that the person is dead, what can I do?"

Anoel said angrily, "Why? Just because I want you to show your authority. You are the king of a country. Shouldn't traitors die?" Louis sighed helplessly, "Ah, if only Wellington would come." Anoel said proudly, "He won't come." Louis sighed again, "It's all because of that boring love affair. Who did that thing?" Suddenly there was a loud noise outside, and the rioting crowd had rushed into the palace!
